Current Commentary

The World Economy Amidst the Turmoil in East Africa

— Liu

The Italo-Abyssinian affair is also a significant event in the world economy. Italy desires to obtain resources from Abyssinia, and is willing to initiate a war for it. However, "weapons are inauspicious." The Italian economy has already been greatly affected by preparations for war. Cash is fleeing, foreign currency is diminishing, and the circulation of bonds and banknotes is expanding daily. Even if it were to gain something after starting a war and prolonging it, it would be difficult to compensate for the losses. Although Italy has rejected the League of Nations' suggestions, the door to peace has not been entirely closed, probably also in view of this situation.

Furthermore, Great Britain is still striving to mediate the war. If it ultimately cannot reverse Mussolini's ambition, it will inevitably be the first to be drawn into the vortex of war. In the London market, the price of U.S. dollars has risen sharply day by day, and the British pound is fleeing. The reason for this is actually the influence of the defense deployments in the Mediterranean. Although the United States is determined to declare neutrality, in such a complex economic situation, even a slight mistake could lead to a repeat of the European war. Therefore, American merchants are extremely sensitive to the Italo-Abyssinian situation. In the New York market, stocks of metals, steel, and military supplies have all risen. American cotton also rose at one point, probably because merchants were concerned that Egyptian and Indian cotton would be damaged by the war. In addition, everything related to military affairs is showing signs of activity. "The arrow maker fears he will not injure people; the armor maker only fears he will injure people." Today's industry and commerce are in just such a situation.

During the European war, Japan took advantage of the opportunity and gained a lot. Taking only the capital of companies as an example, it rose from only 2 billion yen in 1914 to exceeding 10 billion yen in 1922. With the outbreak of the Italo-Abyssinian affair this time, the Japanese business community, with its rich experience, is once again making meticulous plans to reap the fisherman's benefit. Stock, exchange, insurance, and military industries are all making preparations. Even straw sandal merchants are thinking of selling their goods to the Abyssinians, who are accustomed to going barefoot. Japanese commercial operations are able to pay attention to both major and minor details, and are united as a whole to seek foreign development. When opportunities arise, they are unwilling to let them go easily. Is this why they are able to succeed?

Seeing the brewing of the Italo-Abyssinian war, Chinese merchants are also rushing to speculate. Gold labeling, securities, cotton yarn, flour, and wheat market conditions are rising and falling sharply, reaching a temporary peak. If war breaks out unfortunately, in this severe economic situation, how should we deal with ourselves? This is probably not something that these people who are obsessed with speculation have considered. They only want to take the opportunity to make a fortune. They find "watching a fire from across the river" enjoyable, without considering the fear of "a swallow's nest on a dangerous roof." This is truly the most heartbreaking thing. When considering their own interests, why don't our merchants also think about their responsibility to the nation?

Final Mediation Fails; League of Nations in Dire Straits; Special Committee's Negotiations with Italy Yield No Results; Laval Expresses Firm Stance; Will the Rainy Season Prevent War Between Italy and Abyssinia?

(Geneva) The failure of the five-nation special committee to achieve a peaceful resolution of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute has placed the League of Nations in an extremely difficult position. The League of Nations can only choose one of the following two paths now:

(1) Abandon the principles of the League of Nations and allow Italy to do as it pleases;

(2) Uphold the League of Nations Covenant and allow Italy to withdraw from the League of Nations;

It is very difficult for the League of Nations to choose between these two. But, of course, it will be decided by a consensus. After the five-nation special committee met yesterday morning to study the Italo-Abyssinian replies to the committee's suggestions, its chairman, Madariaga, visited Italian chief delegate Aloisi, but the talks yielded no results. According to sources in the League of Nations, Laval's attitude was very firm during the committee meeting yesterday morning. An observer said that Laval's speech took the position of upholding the League of Nations Covenant, and was actually more about being a French foreign minister. Aloisi's remarks during Madariaga's visit could have been published last night, but because the wording needed to be slightly revised, it was decided to postpone it until today.

The five-nation special committee may need two days to draft a report to the League of Nations Council on the failure of the mediation. After this report is submitted, the Council will order the current special committee or a larger committee to formulate suggestions for future proceedings. (Reuters, 24th)

(London) British observers, in view of the end of the rainy season in Abyssinia and Italy's tough stance that the five-nation special committee can no longer carry out its work, hold the view today that the inevitable war between Italy and Abyssinia is not far away. Whether British Ambassador to Italy Drummond's talks with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini last night on behalf of British Foreign Secretary Hoare were the final effort to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian crisis, or, as some parties have reported, only reiterated that the British naval activities in the Mediterranean do not contain any intention to attack Italy, is not yet known. However, it is said that after the five-nation special committee confirmed that the remarks made by Italian representative Aloisi to committee chairman Madariaga were of an official and final nature, it abandoned its mission to mediate the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. Aloisi's remarks against the committee's suggestions were very strong. British representative Eden initially did not believe it was of an official nature, but later learned that the Italian government's opinion was indeed as Aloisi had said, and the committee no longer had any hope of mediation. The British cabinet is scheduled to hold its first plenary meeting since August 22 today. The Times commented on this matter, saying that it would be better not to support the League of Nations than to let the efforts to uphold the League Covenant fail today. If the means of reconciliation or the determination to resist violence pursued by those committed to peace are sacrificed in order to seek the easiest and cheapest way to get rid of difficulties, then it is truly beyond imagination. A Reuters special correspondent in Addis Ababa telegraphed a statement made by a well-known medical expert in Abyssinia, who said that war could not occur for at least a month, because after the end of the rainy season, fevers and cholera would follow, and their momentum would be strong and spread in many places, and could not be eradicated until the end of October. It is said that Italian soldiers are already suffering from fever. Although medical experts say this, observers do not believe that Abyssinia can enjoy another month of peace, unless new efforts at reconciliation in Geneva can succeed quickly. (Reuters, 24th)

British Ambassador Carries Hoare's Letter; Visits Mussolini Again; Secret Talks Last About an Hour

(Rome) British Foreign Secretary Hoare handed a private letter to the Italian Ambassador to Italy, Sir Drummond, to be delivered to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. Tonight, the British Ambassador visited the Italian Prime Minister and talked for about an hour, with no one else present. (Reuters, 23rd)

(Rome) British Ambassador Drummond stated to Mussolini last night that Britain's policy has no anti-Italian inclination. However, the ambassador also told Mussolini that the British government intends to abide by the firm promises under the League of Nations Covenant. (Reuters, 24th)

(London) Last night, British Ambassador to Italy Drummond personally delivered a private letter from British Foreign Secretary Hoare to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. It is said that the nature of the letter was to strengthen the British government's recent public statement regarding British naval actions. Reuters has learned that the letter has received a friendly reply from Mussolini. The London Observer believes that the public statement on British naval actions seems to have had a good effect, and the comments of the Italian newspapers today are more cautious than before, so they are all satisfied. (Reuters, 24th)

Italian Cabinet Announces: No Counter-Proposal Submitted; Response to League of Nations Action Depends on Situation

(Rome) The Italian Cabinet held a meeting today to consider the League of Nations situation and the content of Mussolini's conversation with British Ambassador Drummond last night. A public statement was then issued stating that Italy only verbally stated its reasons for not accepting the five-nation special committee's suggestions, and did not submit a counter-proposal. Everything that has happened since Saturday and Sunday has shown that the Italian government's attitude cannot be regarded as variable. It is said that Mussolini mentioned in today's meeting that the situation has the possibility of developing according to some provisions of the League of Nations Covenant. The Italian government will respond depending on the situation. (Reuters, 24th)

Prime Minister Baldwin Convenes Full Cabinet Meeting; Decision Pending News from All Sides

(London) Prime Minister Baldwin met with several key cabinet members at 10 Downing Street yesterday to prepare for an important full cabinet meeting today to consider the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. Baldwin talked with Lord President MacDonald, Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain, Foreign Secretary Hoare, and Home Secretary Simon for about an hour in the morning. Before the meeting, Baldwin and Hoare had a private conversation for half an hour. In the evening, he returned to have a second conversation with the cabinet members, lasting about ninety minutes. The Ministers of Defense of the Army, Navy, and Air Force all participated. In addition, those present included Foreign Secretary Hoare, President of the Board of Trade Runciman, and Colonial Secretary Malcolm MacDonald. (Reuters, 24th)

(London) The British Cabinet held a full meeting this afternoon, but no public statement was issued after the meeting. With the exception of Eden, who is currently staying in Geneva, all cabinet members attended the meeting and maintained strict secrecy. However, it is known that the cabinet members reviewed the international political situation. The meeting lasted only one hour and forty-five minutes. The British Cabinet is awaiting news from Geneva or telegrams from capitals around the world. Today's cabinet meeting did not have any important discussions. When the meeting will be reconvened has not been decided, but all cabinet members will remain in London so that a special meeting can be convened at any time. (Reuters, 24th)

Five-Nation Committee's Report Nearly Complete; To Be Sent to League of Nations Council for Discussion

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council's Italo-Abyssinian dispute subcommittee held a meeting this morning for two hours. At 12:30 PM, the report was drafted. Its contents include all relevant documents from various negotiations made by the committee since its establishment on September 6. It will be sent to the Council for discussion and the full text will be released this afternoon. The Council will not discuss this report before Thursday, the 26th of this month. The Council intends to know the results of the cabinet meetings held by the British and Italian cabinets today before the meeting. People in the League of Nations believe that there is little hope for substantial progress in the current situation before Thursday. The Council's primary task is to decide what procedures to adopt in the future. Those responsible believe that the procedural issue is secondary. What needs attention most is the future development of the situation, that is, how to deal with the threat of war. (Havas, 24th)

(Geneva) The report of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute subcommittee submitted to the Council was completed this morning. Whether the Council will entrust the committee to draft new proposals will be added in Geneva soon. Optimists believe that the report submitted by the committee does not necessarily mean that mediation efforts have failed. Pessimists believe that the Council will actually handle the Italo-Abyssinian dispute in accordance with the provisions of Article 15 of the League of Nations Covenant. In other words, if Italy violates the obligations stipulated in paragraph 6 of this article, the League of Nations will take sanctions. (Havas, 24th)

(Geneva) The Five-Nation Committee of the League of Nations rejected the request made by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini today. Therefore, Italy's first expression of compromise since the beginning of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute has been unexpectedly rejected. The League of Nations Council will probably hold a meeting on Tuesday or Wednesday to discuss this deadlock. People here believe today that since the Five-Nation Committee has unanimously opposed Italy's request, the Council will probably not propose other solutions. It is expected that the Five-Nation Committee will recommend a subcommittee to draft a report with reference to Article 15 of the League of Nations Covenant. If the League of Nations implements this plan, then Italy's attack on Abyssinia will be completely an act of aggression, and member states should impose sanctions. On the Abyssinian side, because the Abyssinian Emperor notified the League of Nations that he accepted the proposal, his position is no longer in question. (National News Agency, 23rd)

(Geneva) The Five-Nation Committee of the League of Nations has resolved to abandon all hope of mediation. The chairman, Spanish representative Madariaga, announced today that the committee will meet tomorrow to draft a report summarizing the mediation process of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, and delegate the responsibility for the second step of action to the member states. It is understood that the committee intends to publish all the documents of this dispute, including Abyssinia's notification of acceptance of the committee's proposal and Italy's notification of rejection. It is generally believed that this move will force Italy to bear the responsibility for rejecting reconciliation. Since the Five-Nation Committee has abandoned mediation, the entire problem must be resolved by the Council. The Council will also publish a report and propose peace proposals. If Abyssinia accepts the League of Nations' final proposal and Italy still rejects it, then the League of Nations will consider Italy's war against Abyssinia to be illegal. According to the League of Nations Covenant, all member states should help Abyssinia. People here today feel deeply that if Italy does start a war, there is a special intention to impose sanctions. When the Five-Nation Committee met today, French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval criticized Italy's attitude in the capacity of spokesmen for Britain and France, which is noteworthy. Chairman Madariaga asked Italian representative Aloisi whether the proposal put forward by Italy on Sunday was Italy's minimum formal demand. It is said that Aloisi admitted that it was indeed a formal proposal, but it is not yet known whether he said it was the minimum demand. According to Aloisi's answer, if it is true, it conflicts with the statement of the Italian Foreign Ministry spokesperson. The Roman side denied that Italy had submitted a counter-proposal to the Five-Nation Committee. According to news from Addis Ababa, the Abyssinian Foreign Ministry spokesperson said that if Italy had this proposal, it would be "incredible," and that it would be ridiculous to control the Abyssinian army with Italians. (National News Agency, 23rd) (Top right) The Abyssinian Emperor and Empress and their children (Top left) The elite cavalry of Abyssinia (Bottom right) Abyssinian female soldiers holding guns in defensive posture (Bottom left) Italian Prime Minister Mussolini reviews the army

League of Nations Council To Reconvene Tomorrow to Discuss Committee Report

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council will consider the Five-Nation Special Committee's report on Thursday. The committee only completed its work of drafting a comprehensive situation report based on official documents today. (Reuters, 24th)

(Geneva) According to inquiries from Havas' diplomatic correspondent, the future of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute seems very bleak, because the League of Nations Council can no longer make concessions to Italy. When the Council meets tomorrow, it will probably take up the Five-Nation Subcommittee's report on the failure of reconciliation procedures and publish this report so that it can be judged by world opinion. As for whether there is still room for adopting the mediation procedures stipulated in Article 15 of the League of Nations Covenant, it should also be decided by the Council. But in any case, the provisions of Article 16 of the Covenant regarding sanctions cannot be adopted before Italy implements its attack on Abyssinia. Therefore, although mediation has failed, there is still a period of hesitation before Italy starts a war against Abyssinia, and diplomats can still take advantage of this last five minutes to seek a peaceful resolution. This is the only hope for people here. In addition, people from the League of Nations also believe that there is no room for the Five-Nation Subcommittee to continue the mediation process, because since the Three-Nation Conference in Paris, Italy's tone in negotiations has slightly softened, but its fundamental attitude has not changed. If the subcommittee does not follow Italy's wishes, all suggestions will inevitably be rejected by Italy. (Havas, 21st)

Original Text of Five-Nation Committee's Mediation Report To Be Released in Geneva, Divided Into Five Parts

(Geneva) The original text of the Five-Nation Committee's suggestions was released this afternoon, with a total of five major parts. The first part outlines the current situation and the scope of the committee's work. The second part contains several suggestions for reforming Abyssinia. The third part details the implementation of this reform plan. The fourth and fifth parts put forward concrete suggestions for resolving disputes. The first part of the original text states that the committee seeks a basis for negotiations that meets the following conditions: (1) The independence and territorial integrity of the member states; (2) Friendly relations between the member states. It then describes the speech of the Abyssinian representative at the League of Nations Assembly, which stated that Abyssinia is willing to discuss in good faith various suggestions for developing the country's economy, politics, and finance in accordance with the spirit of the League of Nations Covenant.

The second and third parts suggest reforming the following administrative organs: (1) Police; (2) Industry and commerce; (3) Finance; (4) Justice, education, and others. Foreign experts should reform the police administration. The first task of the police is to implement the prohibition of slavery management, carry firearms, and protect the safety of European residences and border areas. Under the outline of economic development, it lists the granting of farming rights and mining rights, the granting of trade rights, and the reform of postal and telecommunications. The financial recommendations include the preparation of budgets, the control of finance, and the study of foreign debt issues. In order to implement this reform, a central bureau should be established. All heads of administrative departments should belong to it. The heads of administrative departments should be foreigners, one of whom is a representative of the League of Nations. The heads of administrative departments should be subject to the control of the administrative commissioner. The administrative commissioner will be the representative of the League of Nations sent to Abyssinia. The last two parts stipulate that the League of Nations special representative should submit a report to the League of Nations at least once a year, and should solicit the opinions of the Abyssinian Emperor beforehand so that the Abyssinian government can add its opinions. The effective period of this plan is five years, and it can be revised based on the experience of the five years. The report then states that the representatives of Britain and France have notified the committee that the two governments are willing to participate in the demarcation of the Italo-Abyssinian border in order to promote the reconciliation of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, and are willing to sacrifice the Somalian coast if necessary to compensate Abyssinia's losses. During the negotiations, the British and French governments will also try to make Abyssinia guarantee the prohibition of the slave system and the arms trade, and are willing to grant Italy special interests in developing Abyssinia's ports. Therefore, the two countries are welcome to sign an economic agreement, but this agreement should respect the rights granted to Britain and France by the people of both countries and existing treaties. (National News Agency, 23rd)

Sanctions Issue; Britain and France Still Negotiating; Laval Met with Eden Again Yesterday

(Geneva) Since arriving here, French Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Laval held talks with representatives of various countries this evening. It is said that what Laval is currently discussing is not only the Abyssinian incident, but also the entire European issue. According to reports, French Ambassador to the United Kingdom Corbin asked the British government a few days ago, saying that since Britain is taking a firm attitude in Geneva on the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, if Central Europe, especially Austria, is invaded in the future, will Britain take the same firm attitude? Regarding this, the British government has not yet replied. This time Laval came to Geneva again, and British Minister without Portfolio Eden may notify Laval of this reply. (Havas, 23rd)

(Paris) According to newspapers here, France's inquiry into Britain's future attitude towards the violation of the League of Nations Covenant by several European countries has become the material for yesterday's talks between Sir Eden and Prime Minister Laval. The two especially considered the issues of signing the Eastern European Pact and guaranteeing Austria's independence. The Daily Telegraph said that Eden told Laval that the British government is prepared to sign most conventions, guaranteeing that Britain and France will continue to actively cooperate in Europe. Eden also said that although there have been many mistakes in British foreign policy in the past few years, recent events have made Britain realize the need to implement a collective security system in both Europe and Africa, so Britain is prepared to undertake this far-reaching obligation. (National News Agency, 23rd)

Italian King Issues Edict; Increases Military Spending for East Africa; Also Issues Three Mobilization Orders

(Rome) Today, the Italian King issued an edict to increase spending on East Africa by 2.5 billion lire, which will be raised in the 1935-36 fiscal year. This includes 1 billion lire for the Ministry of Colonies, 1 billion and 50 million lire for the Ministry of the Army, 150 million lire for the Ministry of the Navy, and 300 million lire for the Ministry of Aviation. Another edict allocates an additional 12 million lire for special emergency highway projects, which is rumored to be used for coastal defense. (Reuters, 23rd)

(Rome) It was announced here today that the mobilization test for all Fascist Party members will begin at 10:00 tomorrow morning. (National News Agency, 23rd)

(Rome) Three orders regarding the mobilization of the Italian army were issued today: one is for reservists from the 1901 to 1914 grades who were exempted from military service for physical reasons to undergo medical examinations again; one allows those under the age of 55 to enlist; and one allows soldiers serving in East Africa to hire people to replace them in marriage ceremonies. (Reuters, 24th)

(Addis Ababa) The Italian Embassy received a report today that an Italian consulate courier traveling between Addis Ababa and Aduwa was arrested by Abyssinian troops. At the same time, Italian consulate personnel in Addis Ababa have been ordered to leave their posts on Saturday. Recently, the Italian Embassy claimed that Abyssinia refused to grant consulate personnel permission to leave the country. The Abyssinian government said that all consulate personnel should be escorted out of the country by government personnel at any time. (National News Agency, 23rd)

Athens The Greek government decided today to lodge a strong protest against Italian ships entering the port of Astypalaia. (National News Agency, 23rd)

Athens According to news here, fifteen British ships will arrive at Corfu tomorrow. Unless something unexpected happens, they will anchor here before October 10. It is also said that this fleet includes a hospital ship, which is the only one seen since the last world war. (National News Agency, 24th)

Malta The new British military commander, Major General McColl, arrived here yesterday and immediately took office. The term of office of the former British military commander, Faulkner, has expired, but he will remain here until he receives instructions from the government. (National News Agency, 24th)

Cairo The Egyptian Ministry of the Army dismissed all Italian employees it had hired on the grounds that there were a large number of Italian expatriates. This matter has aroused great resentment in the Italian community here. The Egyptian side expects Italy to lodge a protest. (National News Agency, 24th)

It seems quite bleak about the prospect before the dispute between Italy and Ethiopia because the Council of the League of Nations is in no position to make any concessions to Italy now. When the Council meets tomorrow, it shall likely take up the reports on the failure of conciliation procedures of the sub-committee composed of five countries, and this set of reports shall be made public for judgment by world opinion. Whether the conciliation procedures as specified in Article 15 of the League's Covenant are worthy of further adoption is up to the Council to decide as well. But, whatever, the provisions of Article 16 on sanctions under the Covenant cannot be adopted before Italy carries out an attack on Ethiopia. The Original Report on the Conciliation by the Five-Nation Committee, To Be Published in Geneva, Altogether Five Parts

(Geneva) The original text of the recommendations of the Five-Nation Committee has been published this afternoon. The content is divided into five major parts. The first part outlines the current situation and the scope of the Committee's work. The second part contains several suggestions for reforming Ethiopia. The third part details the implementation rules of this set of reform plans. The fourth and fifth parts put forward specific suggestions for resolving the dispute. The first part of the original text stated that the committee is trying to find a basis for negotiation that meets the following conditions: (1) the independence and territorial integrity of each member state; (2) friendly relations among the member states. Continuing to outline the speech by a representative from Ethiopia present at the League's General Assembly, it said that Ethiopia is willing to discuss in good faith all kinds of suggestions on developing the country's economy, politics and finance, so as to align with the spirit of the League's Covenant.

The second and third parts suggest reforming the following administration organs: (1) the police, (2) industries and businesses, (3) finance, (4) the judiciary, education, and others. Foreign experts should reform police administration. The first task of the police is to implement the ban on the management of slavery, carrying of firearms, and protection of the safety of European residential areas and border areas. Under the outline of economic development, it lists the granting of cultivated lands and mining areas, the granting of trading rights, and the reforms to posts and telecommunications. The financial recommendations list the compiling of a budget, the control of finances, and the study of external debt issues. For the purpose of implementing this reform, a central bureau should be established. The heads of all administrative departments all belong to it. The heads of all administrative departments should be taken by foreigners, among whom one person is a representative of the League of Nations. The heads of each administrative department should be subject to the control of an administration commissioner, and the administration commissioner will be the representative assigned by the League of Nations to Ethiopia. The last two parts stipulate that the special representative of the League of Nations should submit a report to the League of Nations at least once a year, and should solicit the opinions of the Ethiopian Emperor beforehand so that the Ethiopian government can supplement with its opinions. The effective period of this plan is five years, after which it is open to amend it based on the experience in the five years. The report continues saying that the representatives from the United Kingdom and France have notified the Committee, saying that the two countries' governments are willing to participate in border-setting work between Italy and Ethiopia in order to facilitate a reconciliation of the dispute between Italy and Ethiopia, and if meeting with the necessary, they are also willing to sacrifice coastal land from Somaliland to compensate for the losses of Ethiopia. In the process of the negotiations, the United Kingdom and France will also try to make Ethiopia guarantee to eliminate the system of slavery and arms trade, and are willing to cede the unusual interest in developing Ethiopia's harbors to Italy, therefore the two countries are welcomed to sign an agreement on economy. However, this agreement should respect the rights granted to the people of the two countries and existing treaties from the United Kingdom and France. (National News Agency, 23rd)

Issue of Sanctions; The United Kingdom and France Still Negotiating; Laval Again Meets Eden Yesterday

(Geneva) Ever since French Prime Minister and Foreign Secretary Laval came here, he held dialogues with representatives from various countries this evening. About this layer, the British government has yet to respond. This time, when Laval comes to Geneva again, British Minister without Portfolio Eden may inform Laval of this response. (Havas, 23rd)

Royal Italian Edict Issued; Adding Military Expenditures in East Africa; Also Initiating Three Mobilization Orders

(Rome) Today, the royal Italian edict was issued to add an expenditure of 2.5 billion lira for expenses in East Africa, which will be raised within the fiscal years of 1935 to 1936, and among them including 1 billion lira for colonial department expenses, 1.005 billion lira for the army department expenses, 150 million lira for navy department expenses, 300 million lira for aeronautical department expenses. One allows those younger than the age of 55 to voluntarily enlist. And one allows the soldiers who are leaving to work in East Africa to hire people to stand in for them in their wedding ceremony. Military Contact Between Greece and Turkey; Navies from Both Countries To Be Jointly Exercised

Mockery of Italians: Conspiracy to Help Abdicated King Escape

Ajing: The person in the world most feared by the current Emperor Selassie is the imprisoned abdicated King Iyasu. Recently, there have been rumors of an Italian conspiracy to help him escape, so surveillance has been tightened. Iyasu is the grandson of Emperor Menelik, who defeated the Italian army at Adwa. In 1916, Menelik's daughter, Zewditu, with the support of the current king, usurped the throne from her brother and became empress. After her death, the current king succeeded to the throne and imprisoned Iyasu, where he has been for twelve years. The prison is located in a mountaintop fortress near Harar, with steep cliffs that are difficult to climb. Iyasu has the title of "King of Kings" and is highly revered by Muslims, making him potentially useful to the Italians. However, freeing him from captivity would be extremely difficult. It is said that Iyasu and the guards are bound together by a strong gold chain, so any movement can be detected. The guards have been warned that if the prisoner escapes, they will all face the death penalty. The warden is Abba Hanna, a trusted clergyman of the King, known for his skill in divination. The fortress is surrounded by impenetrable stone walls, with barbed wire fences and alarm bells. Three hundred armed guards patrol at night, assisted by trained police dogs. The King has ordered that Iyasu be treated well and has authorized Abba Hanna to draw funds from the national treasury to meet his needs. The prison furnishings are very exquisite, with various wines, delicacies, a hand-cranked organ, and various books and magazines are provided. He is also allowed female companionship and is "allowed to stroll on the prison lawn under guard." (Reuter Telegram from the North-China Daily News, September 22)

U.S. Senator Borah Advocates Strict Neutrality and Distrusts Anglo-American Cooperation

Boise, USA: Senator Borah delivered a speech to a large crowd here tonight, stating that the United States should be vigilant to avoid being drawn into a European war. The American people unanimously support international peace, but we now understand that Europe still has many important interests that have little to do with the United States. If war breaks out in Europe, many forces will draw the United States into the vortex. Therefore, we should always be vigilant. Britain is now launching a new propaganda campaign in the United States, believing that if Britain is threatened, democracy and world peace are threatened. But we must recognize that their views are only to safeguard their interests. Borah's speech represents the prevailing independent policy in the United States today. (National Telegram, September 23)

American War Veterans Hold Annual Convention

St. Louis: 250,000 American war veterans opened their annual convention here today, lasting four days. The main agenda item for this convention is how to choose between the Reed bill for inflated benefits and the Vincent bill for non-inflated benefits. Both bills were introduced in the last Congress but without result. The American Legion was founded in St. Louis in May 1919. This is the first time in seventeen years that they meet at the point of origin, representatives have also come from the Philippine side, not to mention thousands of representatives coming forward, a grand parade will be held tomorrow, with 15,000 seats arranged along the route to accommodate the audience. (National Telegram, September 23)

U.S. Controls Munitions: Plans to Establish a Licensing System for Management; Committee Held First Meeting Yesterday

(Washington) The National Munitions Inspection Committee, organized by the State Department in accordance with the wartime neutrality law, is scheduled to hold its first meeting tomorrow. Secretary of State Hull recently stated that he could not specify the decisions that the committee could make, but the State Department is eager to establish a licensing system to effectively monitor the manufacture and sale of munitions. Well-informed sources believe that when war breaks out in the future, the list of prohibited exports of various military equipment will be consistent with that proposed by U.S. Ambassador to Switzerland Wilson at the League of Nations Disarmament Conference in Geneva last November, or may even include some raw materials. In short, American public opinion will have a decisive influence on how the list of embargoed items should be formulated. (According to the draft treaty restricting the arms trade submitted by the U.S. representative to the League of Nations Disarmament Conference last November, armaments are divided into five categories: Category 1 includes munitions for land, sea, and air warfare; Category 2 includes naval armaments; Category 3 includes air armaments; Category 4 includes military and non-military ammunition; Category 5 includes ammunition for non-military use but can also be specifically used for military purposes.) (Havas News Agency Telegram, September 23)

Hurricane Strikes Japan: Trees Uprooted and Houses Collapsed Due to Strong Winds

(Tokyo) Western Japan is currently being hit by a hurricane. Yamaguchi Prefecture has been experiencing strong winds since this morning. The connecting ferry between Shimonoseki and Busan has been suspended. In Beppu City, large waves broke through the coastal defenses, and more than 300 houses have been flooded, causing great disorder in the city. Ships to Osaka, Kobe, Hiroshima, and other places have all been delayed. Miyazaki City in Miyazaki Prefecture experienced a strong wind last night, with trees uprooted and power lines cut, plunging the entire city into darkness. The damage to rural areas is significant. According to a report by meteorologist Fujiwara Hiroshi, the hurricane area covers the Nankaido, western China, and Kyushu regions, and its direction is uncertain, moving left or right. Such hurricanes are rare. (Japan Associated Press Telegram, September 24)

Moji: According to a telegram received by the Moji Railway Bureau, the hurricane on the 24th caused considerable damage to various lines in Kyushu. The roof of the platform at the Koshikizaka Station was blown off, and the roofs of the signal station at Miyazaki Station and the Sasebo Station were also blown away by the strong wind. (Japan Associated Press Telegram, September 24)

(Tokyo) At 3:00 PM today, the Central Meteorological Observatory announced that the hurricane is over the sea off Miyazaki Prefecture and is about to make landfall. In the Miyazaki area, the north wind speed is 18 meters per second, and in the Oita area, the northeast wind speed is 10 meters per second. There is heavy rain, and the hurricane will turn to the west-northwest. (Dentsu Telegram, September 24)

Emperor of Abyssinia Releases Prisoners for Military Service

Ajing: The Emperor of Abyssinia has issued a decree releasing prisoners, except for murderers, who volunteer for military service. This move will increase the Abyssinian army by 50,000 men. Many fugitives have also been pardoned, many of whom are brave and have a good record in battle. However, this move by the King also has drawbacks as army commanders now have to implement very strict plans to prevent looting. Hundreds of prisoners have joined Corro's army, totaling 1000 soldiers who have plotted to steal livestock from farmers. Local police are now on high alert. A Reuters reporter has learned from reliable sources that Abyssinia can now mobilize slightly over one million men, but not all of them have rifles. (Reuters Telegram, September 24)

First British Airmail Service to China Via Penang to Hong Kong

(London) The first airmail service from Britain to China began at noon today with an Imperial Airways plane carrying airmail from Croydon Aerodrome. The plane will arrive in Penang in eight days. The mail will then be transferred to another Imperial Airways plane, the *Dorado*, which flew to Penang on September 16th. The *Dorado* will reach its destination . The first test flight to Hong Kong will begin on the day that it disembarks. Mail from here is expected to arrive in China on the 10th. (Reuters Telegram, September 24)

International Commercial Telegraph

——Special Business Telegram from Reuters, September 24——

Gold and Silver:

British Gold: The London gold price today was 144 shillings and 6 pence and has not changed.

British Silver: The London silver market was quiet today, with no movement in either spot or futures prices, remaining at 19 3/3225 pence. The United States and India bought, and China sold. The market closed stable.

Exchange Rates:

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was quiet this morning, with little change in the price of the pound sterling. The British-American exchange rate opened at $4.96625, the same as yesterday's US-British closing price. Within the first hour, it fell 1/875, then rose 1/25 at noon, remaining at $4.915625, with no further changes.

British-French: The opening price rose by 1 pound to 74 francs 57, which remained unchanged until 2:00 PM.

Cotton and Wheat:

US Cotton: The New York cotton market opened unchanged. In the first hour, it rose several points due to the absence of pressure from short selling. It is reported that last week's cotton textile sales exceeded production by 50%.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was stable. At 1:00 PM, the October contract was at 5.87, down two points.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market opened this morning with a feeling of disappointment, but prices recovered slightly due to weather conditions in Argentina. At 1:00 PM, the December contract price was 6 shillings 2 pence 7/875, down 1/25 from yesterday's closing price.

US Wheat: The Chicago market opened today, falling in line with Liverpool, but prices later recovered due to South American telegrams favorable to the bulls, and the strength of suppliers from around the world. Coarse grains opened slightly lower, then recovered in line with wheat prices.

Rubber:

London: The London rubber market was stable this morning. At noon, the transaction price for the January-March contract was 5 pence 6/875, up 0.0625 from yesterday's closing price.

New York: Rubber opened higher by 60 points in New York as a result of the International Rubber Regulation Committee's decision to reduce the export quota for the last two months of this year to 60%. The committee had resolved on March 26th that the export quota for the second half of this year would be 65%, but has now revised the previous resolution. Although there was some profit-taking, the market was still strong after the price increase.

Securities:

New York: The New York Stock Exchange opened slightly higher, and the market continued to be stable, showing sympathy with London. Oil stocks hovered around yesterday's closing price, and other securities rose. Among mining stocks, steel stocks were still in higher demand. Automobile, railway, and public utility stocks were all still strong. The Dow Jones average of 31 industrial stocks opened at 130.02, up 47 points. Various prices are listed on the left.

Ministry of Communications Plans to Issue Telecommunications Bonds

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications plans to issue 10 million yuan in telecommunications bonds to reorganize the telegraph and telephone systems. The draft issuance regulations and repayment schedule have been passed by the Central Political Council and submitted to the Legislative Yuan. After review and approval by the Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan, it can be passed by the General Assembly this week and issued on the first day of next month. The revenue of the International Telecommunications Bureau, after deducting the principal and interest of the British Gengkuan loan, will be used as the repayment fund for the bonds. If insufficient, monthly allocations will be made from postal and telecommunications revenue to supplement it. (Special dispatch, 24th)

(Nanjing) Regarding the Ministry of Communications' plan to issue 10 million yuan in telecommunications bonds in the 24th year of the Republic of China, after being approved by Sun Ke and submitted to the Finance Committee for review, it is now known that the Legislative Yuan has decided to issue this bond on October 1st, and plans to complete the review within this week and submit it to the Yuan meeting for announcement. This bond is to be used for expanding and reorganizing the telegraph, telephone, and wireless radio systems. The annual interest rate is 6%, and it will be repaid in seven and a half years. Principal and interest will be repaid at the end of each month in March, June, September, and December through the Bank of China. The revenue from international telegraph fees under the Ministry of Communications, after deducting the principal and interest of the Sino-British Gengkuan Board of Directors, will be used as collateral. Any shortfall will be supplemented from other postal and telecommunications revenue. (Central News Agency dispatch, 24th)

Tianjin Hengyuan Factory to Resume Production, Managed by Bank Consortium

Tianjin Correspondence: Since the Hengyuan Yarn Factory was taken over and managed by the creditor banks China, Central, Jin City, and Continental, which organized a creditor group based on their creditor status, Zeng Xiangxi, the manager of Shanghai Shenxin Yarn Factory No. 7, was hired to serve as the representative in Tianjin and stationed at the factory to implement management. Preparations began a month ago. Improvements to technology, repairs to machinery, renovation of houses, and addition of new machines are nearing completion. The newly purchased German Escher Wyss factory and Japanese Toyoda textile machinery parts, totaling 60 horsepower, have arrived in Tianjin and are being installed. The newly ordered 400 Escher Wyss looms are on their way and are expected to arrive in Tianjin next month. The factory has been shut down for nearly a year, and more than 2,700 workers have lost their jobs. Some have been forced by poverty to become thieves, adding to social unrest. The resumption of work will have a positive impact on society directly and indirectly. In order to thoroughly reform and increase work efficiency, the factory has hired Li Rongguang, Zeng Ze, and Wan Chengzhi, graduates of the Tokyo Higher Institute of Technology, to manage the yarn spinning, machinery, and electrical departments, respectively. All operations will be modernized, with electric motors converted to small motors. The factory will only employ 1,500 workers, and some female workers will be used because female workers are more patient, meticulous, and can increase work efficiency. Workers from the Shanghai Shenxin Yarn Factory will be transferred north to work when necessary. When the original 1,700 workers were laid off, an agreement was signed stating that the factory must give priority to hiring the old workers whenever the factory resumes production. The matter was filed with the Tianjin Social Affairs Bureau. Therefore, although the factory intends to eliminate some old workers, it is difficult to announce due to concerns about causing unexpected incidents. The resumption date is scheduled for the end of October, when new cotton becomes available.

After the Hengyuan factory resumes production, Tianjin's industry will add some new vitality. Three of the six major yarn factories in North China remain, and they will not be completely monopolized and absorbed by Japanese yarn. The scale of the Yuyuan Yarn Factory was originally the largest of the six major yarn factories. It shut down this spring, owing 6 million in foreign debt, especially to Japanese creditors. Shareholders' meetings were held repeatedly, and it was decided to liquidate the factory, sell the entire factory to repay the old debts, raise new capital, or reorganize a new shareholders' meeting to take over the factory and borrow capital from the bank consortium to resume operations. The Economic Commission may assist with valuation. However, although the liquidation has been completed, there is no capital for resumption, and no arrangements have been made to offset the old debts. The person in charge of the factory is in Shanghai negotiating with the banking community, but has not yet made any progress. The banking community believes that the factory cannot repay its previous debts, and its production equipment cannot offset the debts. Since North China's yarn factories have been affected by Japanese yarn, even if they are restored, it will be difficult to compete. It is dangerous to invest in loans, so they are reluctant to help Yuyuan resume operations. The resumption of the Hengyuan Yarn Factory is an attempt by the banking community to provide assistance to industry. If it is effective, it may be further extended to Yuyuan. (20th)

Guangdong Eastern Defense Army Searches and Suppresses Bandits on the Guangdong-Fujian Border, Raoping Attacks Security Team for Four Nights, Yang Battalion Captures Fake Team Leader and Secretary

The bandits on the Guangdong-Fujian border have been appearing and disappearing unpredictably recently. Raoping County, Guangdong Province, which borders Fujian, has recently discovered bandits. The county's security team and defense army have stepped up suppression. However, on the evening of the 2nd of this month, dozens of bandits with dozens of rifles and pistols were discovered in Ganyu Village, Twelfth Pai, Wuzhi Township, District 5 of the county, attempting to attack the second squad of the security team stationed in the Qiushi Ancestral Hall in the village. Fortunately, they were discovered by a sentry, who immediately sounded the gong to gather the crowd and pursue them separately. The bandits resisted by fighting and retreating, throwing hand grenades. When the main force of the military police arrived to encircle and suppress them, the bandits had already fled far away. The Zeng Youren Brigade of the First Independent Division stationed in Raoping believed that the bandits were rampant and immediately dispatched Battalion Commander Yang to lead his troops to search the bandit area. On the 9th of the month, Battalion Commander Yang led the entire battalion in six routes to encircle Phoenix Mountain, burning several bandit strongholds in the Qiaokeng mountain forest, killing more than 30 bandits, and capturing the local bandit secretary and finance chief, who were executed on the spot and their heads were displayed to the public. On the evening of the 20th, at about 11 pm, Battalion Commander Yang received a report from the gentry that the bandits in Dashan had recently established a secret agency in Jiaoshuikeng, plotting wrongdoing. Battalion Commander Yang dispatched a team to suppress them. When they arrived at the destination, it was already the third watch of the night. They found lights in the forest, knowing it was a bandit secret cave. They sent troops to charge forward and encircle and suppress them in separate routes. The bandits also resisted stubbornly, and the gunshots shook the valley. After about half an hour of confrontation, the bandits ran out of ammunition and fled, abandoning their weapons. However, the mountains were deep and the forests were lush, and the intersections were numerous. The defense army was afraid of being tricked by the bandits and did not pursue them deeply. They simply set the bandit agency on fire. Before long, the east was already white. They began to search separately, finding five bandit corpses outside the agency gate. After searching in the deep forest, they captured two bandits alive. One, surnamed Liu, was the fake detachment leader of the bandits, and the other, surnamed Chen, was the detachment secretary of the bandits. They were immediately escorted back to the battalion headquarters and transferred to the brigade headquarters for interrogation. (September 19)

Wuxi: The Zhenxin Dispute Fully Resolved

The Zhenxin Yarn Factory labor-management dispute had reached an impasse due to both sides taking extreme positions. Subsequently, Provincial Party Committee member Pan Guojun came to Wuxi to investigate the truth. He consulted with the County Party Committee, the county government, and the Chamber of Commerce. As factory manager Jiang Zhexian was ill in Shanghai, he immediately arranged for County Party Committee member Sun Xiangfeng, Chamber of Commerce executive committee member Sun Qing, Director of the Chengxi Social Service Center Tang Pu'an, Textile Industry Association member Xue Mingjian, and others to go to Shanghai. They repeatedly and earnestly consulted with Zhenxin manager Jiang Zhexian, staff member Shao Chun, Li Yunhou of the Shanghai Bank, Tan Senshou of the Wuxi branch, and others. It was decided that Zhenxin would raise 5,300 yuan for worker savings deposits and 3,000 yuan for worker bonuses, to be handed over to the Chamber of Commerce for distribution by the County Party Committee. The August salaries owed to staff would be resolved by the factory itself. As there was a concrete solution, Committee member Pan and others returned to Wuxi the night before last to report to County Magistrate Wang. All staff and workers have agreed to the arrangement. The total amount of 8,300 yuan in worker funds was sent to the Chamber of Commerce yesterday for immediate distribution. The August salaries owed to staff have also been paid. Thus, the factory's labor unrest has been fully resolved. It is reported that the internal management has also reached an agreement with the Shanghai Bank, and work is expected to resume soon. Additionally, the Lihua Village Yukan Yarn Factory, which had been shut down for three months due to its inability to sustain operations by selling yarn, has also found a solution. With the new cotton season arriving, it has been decided that work will resume in two weeks.

Nantong: Langshan Monk Nearly Subjected to Autopsy

An unidentified male corpse was found on Chengnan Park Road, with a Buddhist tonsure on his head but wearing secular clothing. Students from the Nantong Medical University obtained permission from the court to perform an autopsy for experimental purposes. The procuratorate first issued a public notice seeking relatives to claim the body. On the 23rd, Ren Gui came forward to identify the deceased as his brother, a monk at Langshan Monastery with the Dharma name Jicheng. The procuratorate dispatched police to the medical school, where the body was removed from the preservative solution and handed over to Ren Gui for coffining and burial.

Hangzhou: Zhejiang Salt Workers Petition to Resume Salt Collection

Salt collection has been suspended at salt fields in Yuyao and other locations in the five Zhejiang eastern prefectures. Representatives from the county's Salt Industry Workers' Union, along with over seventy salt workers from various districts, came to Hangzhou to petition the Provincial Party Committee, the provincial government, and the Salt Transport Bureau. The various agencies recognized that this matter concerned the livelihood of 100,000 salt workers and gave it great importance. The Transport Bureau has already ordered the Songjiang salt warehouse to instruct the factory to resume collection. While the Zhejiang eastern warehouse has secured funds, it insists on reducing the quota. The salt workers have expressed their inability to accept this, and the two sides remain in disagreement.

Wang Kemin Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning, Meets with Journalists in the Afternoon, Scheduled to Visit Huang Fu in Moganshan Tomorrow Morning

According to the Central News Agency, former Acting Chairman of the Executive Yuan's Political Affairs Readjustment Committee in Beiping, Wang Kemin, left Beiping to travel south due to the Committee's closure. He is to report to President Wang on the closure and also must visit Huang Fu in Moganshan, the former chairman of the Committee, to report. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning and scheduled a meeting with reporters from various local newspapers in the afternoon. Details are as follows:

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning: After arriving in Nanjing from Beiping, Wang Kemin reported everything to President Wang. As the closure of the Committee needs to be reported to Chairman Huang, he traveled to Shanghai the night before last with Tang Erhe, Zhou Jingzhai, and three others on the overnight express train. They arrived at the North Station in Shanghai at 7:15 yesterday morning and went directly to the residence of Wang's younger sister on Yuyuan Road to rest. Having been away from Shanghai for a long time, he has private matters to attend to and has decided to stay in Shanghai for two days.

Departing for Hangzhou Tomorrow Morning: Wang Kemin has decided to take the early express train from Shanghai to Hangzhou at 8:00 AM on the 26th. After staying in Hangzhou for a day, he will go to Moganshan to visit former Chairman of the Political Affairs Readjustment Committee Huang Fu to report on his time as acting chairman, the closure of the Committee, and the recent situation in North China. He will stay in Moganshan for at most one night before returning to Hangzhou to handle family funeral matters and to stay in Hangzhou for several days to build a tomb. Then, he will come to Shanghai. In the future, he will travel between Nanjing, Beiping, and Shanghai.

Statement to the Press: At 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon, Wang Kemin met with reporters from various newspapers at his younger sister's residence on Yuyuan Road and made the following statement: The situation regarding the closure of the Executive Yuan's Political Affairs Readjustment Committee in Beiping has been reported in the press. In the future, all political affairs in North China that fall within the scope of local matters will be handled separately by the Hebei Provincial Government and the Tianjin Municipal Government. Other important matters will be handled by the central government. The situation in North China has improved compared to before. The abolition of the Political Affairs Readjustment Committee in Beiping is also due to the more stable situation in North China. A report on the Committee's work from its beginning to its closure will be submitted by the Executive Yuan to the Sixth Plenary Session. He has met with President Wang and Minister of Military Affairs He in Nanjing. He has not heard about Minister He's return to the north. He will visit Huang Yingbai in Moganshan on the 26th to report on the situation in North China and the closure of the Political Affairs Readjustment Committee in Beiping. After a short stay, he will go to Hangzhou to handle private matters. Wang Kemin went on to say that the Hebei Economic Association, organized by leaders from the banking and industrial sectors of Beiping and Tianjin, is purely a research institution. All economic issues related to Hebei will be discussed by the Association to revive Hebei's declining economy. The issue of economic cooperation between China and Japan has only been seen in rumors, and there has been no contact between the two sides so far.

Li Zeyi Returned to Shanghai from Japan Yesterday

According to the Central News Agency, Senior Advisor to the Fujian Provincial Government Li Zeyi traveled to Japan earlier this month to visit friends. The ship was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 3:00 PM yesterday, but due to heavy winds and waves outside Wusongkou, it was delayed until 7:00 PM. Many of Li's relatives and friends went to welcome him. According to Li's statement to reporters on the ship, his trip to Japan was to mourn the late Sugiyama Shigemaru and had no other purpose. Sugiyama was the leader of Toyama Mitsuru's Genyosha in Japan and had contributed to the Meiji Restoration. He passed away at the age of 72. As an old friend of many years, he went to mourn him. While in Japan, he also visited Vice Minister Shigemitsu and Major General Okamura, but these were only ordinary friendly visits. During his stay in Shanghai, he plans to stay for a few days and visit Huang Fu, whom he has not seen in a long time. He also plans to go to Nanjing, but the dates are not yet determined.

Factory Operations Mortgage Loan; Outline of Implementation Drafted; Seeking Opinions from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for Reference; Scheduled to be Submitted to the Standing Committee for Discussion on the 27th

The Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Committee decided to allocate 3 million yuan from the credit small loan fund borrowed from various banks and money shops to handle operational mortgage loans in order to support industry. The chairman of the committee, Cai Zengji, has now drafted a plan and sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce seeking opinions. A meeting of the Standing Committee is scheduled for 4:00 PM on the 27th to discuss the matter. Details are as follows:

Seeking Opinions from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: Cai Zengji adopted various opinions and drafted appropriate measures. In addition to sending a special letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce leaders in industry and commerce to seek opinions, he also hopes that industrialists and economists will express their views for reference. A letter was sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating: "Regarding the decision made at the first meeting of our committee to allocate 3 million yuan of national currency from the industry and commerce credit small loan fund borrowed from name-brand banks and money shops to handle operational mortgage loans for domestic goods factories in order to support industry, a draft outline for handling this loan has been prepared to be submitted for discussion at the meeting this Friday and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval. Fearing that the proposed plan may not be appropriate, we are sending ten copies of the mimeographed version and request that you review them and distribute them to relevant member associations of your chamber for reference. If you have any insightful suggestions, please submit them in writing to our committee by this Friday so that we may consider them. Respectfully, Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee."

Draft Outline for Mortgage Loans: Factory Operations Mortgage Loans

Draft Outline for Handling Mortgage Loans: (1) To assist the review committee, encourage production, and maintain the livelihood of workers, it was submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval to allocate funds from the industry and commerce credit small loan fund borrowed from various banks and money shops, and the borrowed fund will continue to be partially secured by national treasury bonds. (2) (3) The application period for this loan is set for two weeks each time, until the 3 million yuan is loaned out. (4) Domestic goods factories, original machinery, and factory buildings must be indispensable and can apply for loans with appropriate collateral. (5) For raw materials, manufactured goods needed in the market can apply for loans with appropriate collateral. (6) Goods that have been manufactured but not yet sold and are stored in warehouses can be used as collateral to apply for loans if they are identified as needed and valuable in the market. (7) Domestic goods factories with solid assets but lacking the minimum working capital can apply for loans with appropriate collateral. (8) Factories that contract for projects and need working capital before the project payments are received can apply for loans with the phased payment contract for the project as collateral. The materials already purchased or to be purchased will be used as part of the collateral and cannot be used for other purposes. The receivables should be collected by our committee and deposited with the bank for safekeeping. (9) The collateral for this loan shall be subject to the provisions of Articles 6 and 7 of the Loan Detailed Rules. (10) The loan amount shall not exceed 60% of the current market price or valuation of the collateral. (11) The collateral is limited to the first mortgage right, but if the borrowing factory obtains the consent of the first mortgage creditor to transfer the priority to this chapter, the rules shall apply. (14) This mortgage loan shall be handled in accordance with banking practices. (15) This outline shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Ministry of Finance.

Chamber of Commerce Soliciting Factory Opinions: The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a notice to relevant factory associations seeking opinions on factory operations loans, stating: "Regarding the letter approved by the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee on the 23rd of this month, at yesterday's 12th meeting, a majority of committee members unanimously proposed that the credit small loan has been helpful to small industries and businesses for nearly two months. In order to actively promote relief, we request that a considerable amount be allocated from the credit loan fund to be used as a factory operations loan, so as to support industry, encourage production, and maintain the livelihood of workers. It was resolved to allocate 3 million yuan from the credit small loan fund recognized by various banks and money shops as a domestic goods factory operations mortgage loan. Chairman Cai was appointed to draft detailed measures to be submitted to the meeting for discussion and decision next Friday, and then submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval and implementation. It has been recorded. Now, the planning of this factory operations loan has been started by Chairman Cai of our committee. In order to gather ideas and make the plan appropriate for implementation, we intend to ask your association to express your insightful opinions and forward them to the factory associations of various industries to submit their opinions as much as possible in writing to our association before the early hours of the 26th of this month for reference. We hereby notify you and hope that you will investigate and handle the matter and reply. With this, in addition to submitting to the Industry and Commerce Revitalization Committee of this association for comments, we hereby notify you to inspect the matter and provide any comments on the above plan in writing by Wednesday of this week for verification and handling. We look forward to it."

Amidst the Decline of All Industries, the Silk Industry Suddenly Becomes Active; Due to a Sharp Increase in Demand from Europe and America, the Prices of Cocoons, Silk, and Satin All Rise

Recently, while all industries are in decline, the silk industry has suddenly shown signs of prosperity. Due to a sharp increase in demand from Europe and America, the price of raw silk has soared overseas. According to a report from the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, Shanghai's raw silk exports were 3,588 bales in June, increased to 5,800 bales in July, and further increased to 6,981 bales in August, an increase of about one time compared to June. The market price of high-quality Shanghai white factory silk in August was 580 yuan per picul, and the market price of high-quality Sichuan yellow factory silk was 460 yuan, an increase of 14% and 21% respectively compared to 510 yuan for factory silk and 380 yuan for yellow factory silk in July. With the brisk sales of silk and the depletion of silk inventories, various silk factories have increased production, requiring a large number of cocoons, and the price of cocoons has risen sharply. The market price per picul has risen from 72 yuan in July to 85 yuan this month. The export of waste silk is also quite prosperous, with 1,210 bales in June, 1,714 bales in July, and a further increase to 2,467 bales last month, an increase of more than double compared to June. The market prices of silk and crepe have also risen accordingly.

Xi'an will open on Tuesdays and Fridays, and Chengdu will open on Wednesdays and Saturdays. The flight dates and times are connected to the Shanghai-Xi'an section of the Shanghai-Xinjiang route, with Nanjing, Zheng County, Xi'an, and Hanzhong as intermediate stops. It will depart from Shanghai at 6:30 AM every Tuesday and Friday morning and arrive in Xi'an at 1:20 PM on the same day and in Chengdu at 5:00 PM. It will fly back from Chengdu at 8:00 AM every Wednesday and Saturday morning and arrive in Xi'an at 11:00 AM and in Shanghai at 6:15 PM. All postal items going to each station on the route will be sealed and shipped by this bureau at 10:00 PM every Monday and Thursday. We hereby notify the public to be aware.

A Dispute Arises Over the Mortgage of the Jinxing Mansion; The Banking and Money Industries Decide to Assist Various Banks and Money Shops

According to the Central News Agency, the economic downturn has dealt a fatal blow to Shanghai's real estate developers, and this is another concrete proof. The Jinxing Real Estate Company, founded and operated by the famous real estate developer Sun Chunsheng, has recently caused a dispute between Chinese, British, and Japanese businessmen over the mortgage of its Jinxing Mansion at the end of its resources. According to investigations by reporters from the Central News Agency:

7 Million Yuan Mortgaged Over the Years

The Jinxing Mansion, owned by Jinxing Real Estate Company, has been mortgaged over the years to the Central Trust Company, Yisheng, Xinfu, Henglong, Hongsheng, Shenyuan, Tongqing, and other money shops for a total of 7 million yuan. Last year, when real estate prices in Shanghai fell, the company stopped paying interest. In order to protect the debt, the creditors applied to the First Special District Court to have the rent of the mortgaged houses pre-emptively attached and ordered the tenants to pay the rent to the creditors for deposit with the court.

British and Japanese Businessmen Suddenly Start Collecting Rent

Then, the British business Yexing Real Estate Company came forward to forcibly collect rent, claiming that they had obtained a long-term lease right for the houses from Jinxing Real Estate Company. The Central Trust Company filed a lawsuit with the court based on the facts and submitted evidence proving the forgery of Yexing Company's lease. After the court rejected Yexing Company, a Japanese man named Okamoto Otoichi, using the name of Murakami Law Office, hired a Japanese person to come forward to forcibly collect rent, claiming that Yexing had mortgaged the long-term lease from Jinxing to Okamoto for 800,000 yuan. The houses have now been assigned to Okamoto to collect rent. However, the tenants have seen through the scheme and are still legally submitting the rent to the banks and money shops designated by the court for safekeeping. At present, Yexing Company has already been rejected in the first instance, but has appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court.

The Banking and Money Industries Decide to Assist: In order to protect the legitimate rights of various banks and money shops, the Shanghai Banking and Money Industries Association held a joint meeting of the banking and money industries at the Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation at 5:00 PM yesterday to discuss everything. Those who attended the meeting included Tang Zhimin, Hu Xian, Zhuang Dezhi, Qin Runqing, Xu Jiqing, Wang Boyuan, Lu Yunqing, Yi Zhizi, Jing Runshi, Wang Huaimi, Xi Jiming, Yu Zuoting, Wu Weiruru, Hu Bijiang, Bei Songsun, Qu Jigang, Ye Fuxiao, and others, totaling more than ten people. This case will affect the financial industry and they will provide assistance.

Memorial Submitted to the Ministry by the General Association of Merchant Ship Masters: Before the Establishment of a Maritime Court, Courts Handling Collision Cases Should Invite Maritime Experts for Consultation

The General Association of Merchant Ship Masters has submitted a memorial to the Ministry of Transportation, requesting that the Ministry consult the Ministry of Justice. Before a maritime court is established, when courts hear ship-related cases, they should invite maritime experts to consult together to clarify responsibilities and avoid unjust imprisonments. It has been investigated that on the evening of April 22nd of this year, the Haizhou vessel of the China United Company, returning to Shanghai, encountered the Huang Youlan barge while entering the port near Lujiazui. The barge had no lights, did not heed warnings, and was operated by a drunken sailor who recklessly charged ahead, disregarding the danger. This left the Haizhou vessel with no room to maneuver in a navigationally challenging area. The barge continued to ram the Haizhou vessel, leading to the disaster where the cook, Liu Qi, tragically died due to excessive drinking. Both parties requested adjudication from the Shanghai Maritime Bureau's Ship Collision Dispute Resolution Committee. Simultaneously, Huang Youlan filed a criminal self-accusation with the court. When the committee made its adjudication, it deemed the responsibility to lie with the barge but, considering the death of the barge operator, suggested a slight compensation for relief. Therefore, the committee determined that the Haizhou vessel bore 30% of the responsibility for the compensation. The barge side, also aware of their fault, felt grateful for the relief they received. The case was closed, and the self-accusation was withdrawn from the court. However, the court, in hearing the case, disregarded the committee's adjudication and sentenced the captain of the Haizhou vessel, Zheng Runru, to imprisonment, which is extremely surprising. The reasoning behind the judgment was that there were lights on the mast of the barge, and the captain failed to notice them. The captain also failed to understand the ebb and flow of the tide, committing a negligent homicide in the course of duty, punishable by three years of imprisonment. Upon investigation, barges in the port of Shanghai do not have masts. How could lights be hung? Furthermore, Huang Youlan admitted to not having lights. What does the claim of lights on the mast refer to? The Haizhou vessel, entering the port against the tide during low tide, reduced its speed, adhering to the regulations for navigation. What is the basis for claiming a misunderstanding of the ebb and flow of the tide? It is clear that the boat owner is unjustly suffering a wrongful verdict. Our association believes that piloting ships is a specialized skill. In law, there are international navigation regulations, local navigational rules, and maritime law that constrain operations. Physically, there are influences such as wind, tides, weather, waterway changes, inertia, and the speed and maneuverability of the machinery and rudder. The primary aim of investigating ship collisions is to determine responsibility. However, responsibility is not solely based on the party suffering damage. Sometimes, even if a boat capsizes and people die, the party may still bear responsibility for causing the accident. Therefore, investigating ship collision cases requires someone with profound maritime experience to competently fulfill the role. This is why advanced maritime nations have maritime courts. Although the establishment of a maritime court in our country has been approved by the administrative conference, it has not yet been established. While your ministry has designated the organization of ship collision dispute resolution committees in various port maritime bureaus, parties involved can still file lawsuits with the court. Judges, lacking maritime expertise, openly make independent judgments, making it difficult to avoid wrongful verdicts and unjust imprisonments. If this continues without remedial measures, cases like that of Captain Qin will become commonplace. Sailors will feel a sense of shared grief and view the helm with fear,不敢問津矣. Considering that your ministry is the central authority for our sailors, it should devise comprehensive strategies to protect the legal rights of sailors. Therefore, we jointly submit this memorial to your ministry, requesting that you swiftly establish a maritime court as a fundamental solution. Additionally, we request that you consult the Ministry of Justice to ensure that, before a maritime court is established, courts handling ship-related cases invite several maritime experts who have served as captains for three or more years to consult together as a temporary remedy. We also request that you forward this request to the Ministry of Justice, ordering the High Court to invite experts to jointly hear the appeal of Zheng Runru's case to redress the injustice. Implementing this would be a virtuous act. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Transportation.

First Batch of Autumn Cocoons from Jiangsu Province: Over a Thousand Loads Arrived Yesterday; Total Yield Estimated at Over Fifty Thousand Loads

After the autumn cocoons matured in areas such as Wuxi, Changzhou, and Suzhou in Jiangsu Province, over ten silk factories in this city, including Jincheng, Youli, Baotai, and Fuxing, went to collect the cocoons and have now completed their task. Yesterday, Mr. Pu Xin-kuan of the Jincheng Silk Factory told a reporter from the Shih Yeh Pao that the cocoon harvest in the Wuxi area this autumn was slightly better than in Zhejiang Province but only half of the spring cocoon harvest. It is estimated that the autumn cocoon yield is only over 100,000 loads, with 70-80% already collected by local manufacturers, leaving only 20-30% purchased by manufacturers in this city. The purchase price is around 22 yuan per load. Because of the significant wastage during silk reeling (over 400 catties of dry cocoons yield one load of silk), the factory can barely cover expenses and has no profit to gain. The supply of dry cocoon raw materials in Shanghai, including the 10-20% collected from Zhejiang, can only last until the beginning of December. After that, due to a lack of raw materials, factories will have to cease operations one after another. The reason for the insufficient supply of raw materials is that silk prices have been too low in recent years, and cocoon prices have plummeted, making it difficult for villagers to make a living. Therefore, they have collectively converted mulberry fields to grow grains. Due to the lack of raw materials for raising silkworms, the cocoon yield has also decreased significantly. Today, manufacturers transported over 1,000 loads of autumn cocoons from Wuxi and Changzhou to Shanghai, including over 200 loads from Jincheng, over 200 loads from Youli, over 400 loads from Fuxing, and over 200 loads from Baotai. Fresh cocoons from various regions will continue to be transported to Shanghai in batches for use.
