Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Clarifies: Member Certificates Do Not Require Stamp Duty

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce received a letter from the Tianjin Customs Broker Association inquiring whether the new regulations stipulate that the member certificates of industry associations are exempt from stamp duty. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce immediately responded, stating that Article 16, Clause 28 of the Stamp Tax Law refers to certificates issued by competent government agencies to certify the identity or qualifications of individuals. Certificates issued to members by commercial organizations are not examples of competent government agencies certifying the identity or qualifications of individuals. Therefore, such certificates do not require stamp duty.

Shipping Companies Decide to Petition in Beijing: Requesting Revision of Stamp Tax Rates

The Shanghai Shipping Guild believes that the newly promulgated stamp tax regulations, which require a stamp duty of two jiao for each bill of lading for ship cargo, have increased significantly from the original and deviate from the standard practice of tax levies. In some cases, the freight revenue for a single document is only 5 jiao, and after deducting customs declaration fees and commissions, the shipping company will have no income left after paying the stamp duty. Shipping companies had previously submitted a request to the Central Legislative Yuan to amend the regulations. As there has been no definite solution yet, shipping companies are finding it difficult to cope. Therefore, yesterday, the 5th Executive Committee meeting was convened to discuss the issue of stamp tax rates on ship bills of lading. As a result of the meeting, it was decided that the guild would draft a memorial and appoint Chu Zhiqing, chairman of the Shanghai Shipping Guild, standing committee member Yuan Yideng, and committee member Wang to petition the Legislative Yuan in Beijing. They will request that the new stamp tax rates for bills of lading be amended and new rates be set. Furthermore, regarding the previous resolution by the guild to suspend the collection of surcharges for the Wusong Merchant Marine School, the Ministry has replied, disapproving the suspension. This issue was also submitted to the Executive Committee for discussion. As a result, it was decided to continue the request and publicly appoint the chairman and the two standing committee members, Wang and Yuan, to clarify the situation to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Communications, and the Ministry of Finance during their petition in Beijing. They will strive to achieve the goal of suspending the surcharges.

Yuyao Salt Farmer Representatives Arrive in Shanghai: Make Various Requests for Assistance

The Yuyao salt farmers have traditionally been able to negotiate fair prices for their salt with mountain merchants, who have exclusive rights to purchase and sell the salt. However, this spring, two major manufacturers from eastern and western Zhejiang established a salt merchant association in Hangzhou, forming an alliance to cut off salt purchases. The price was reduced from 8.4 jiao per dan to 6 jiao per dan, causing great hardship for the tens of thousands of salt farmers in the area. Subsequently, the Party and government authorities mediated, and both sides compromised, delaying the matter for two months. Fortunately, it was eventually determined that the annual salt price would be 8 jiao per dan, and the salt field office was notified to inform everyone. However, the merchants have been insincere in implementing this government order. They purchase the salt but do not pay for it, claiming that the market is sluggish and that they lack sufficient funds. All the factories have secretly formed an alliance and unanimously announced the suspension of salt purchases. Despite repeated negotiations by the salt farmers, no results have been achieved after three months. The salt barns are empty, livelihoods have been cut off, and suffering is immense. Instability is inevitable and is worsening daily. The Salt Farmers' Union held a meeting and, recognizing that the unresolved issue could harm local governance, specially dispatched over ten representatives from various districts to petition Party and government agencies and the Salt Transport Office in Zhejiang. On the 21st, over twenty salt farmers from various districts of the county, including Lu Chenghui, Shen Chengjiong, Yuan Gongqi, Yu Liyou, Shen Dayou, Xiang Xizhi, and Shen Bairong, arrived in Shanghai on behalf of over ten thousand salt farmers in the county. They presented a brief to the Ningbo Shaoxing fellow-countrymen associations and prominent figures in Shanghai, such as Yu Qiaqing and Song Hanzhang, requesting their support and assistance to save the lives of tens of thousands of people on the verge of starvation. The main points of the brief are: (1) urge the Salt Bureau to pay attention to the livelihood of salt farmers and local security; (2) order Wang Shoushan, general manager of Zhejiang West Yuantai Company and other salt merchants, and Gu, chairman of Zhejiang East Company, to expedite the purchase of the quota of salt and pay for it.

Relief Efforts in Tianmen by the Jisheng Society

The China Jisheng Society recently received a letter from Hou Ruide and Qian Xinru, the heads of the association's Tianmen County branch, reporting that they arrived in Tianmen on the 19th of this month with relief workers and designated Dongmen Diyan No. 2 as a temporary relief station. Their plan is to thoroughly investigate households in the most severely affected areas and provide tickets to the extremely poor to prevent corruption. If relief rice is needed, it can be purchased from nearby Jingmen and Yingcheng counties, where the price is cheaper. The Tianmen dou is larger than the Fancheng dou by two, so each dou can be increased by six sheng of the Hanhu dou. The price is approximately six yuan and two jiao per stone in Han currency. Broad beans cost two yuan and five jiao per shi, which is equivalent to one yuan and two jiao per Hanhu. They are currently conducting investigations. They have encountered disaster victims reporting that the flood has inundated all the surrounding villages and submerged the city, resulting in the drowning of approximately 200,000 people. Everywhere the directors went, disaster victims wailed and begged for relief, their cries shaking the heavens. Corpses littered the ground. They urgently request additional relief funds to save the remaining lives and prevent them from filling the ditches.

Three Businesses Announce Liquidation Due to Poor Market Conditions

Renji Iron Works

The Renji Iron Works in the Southern City has been in business for over a decade. Its business has generally been quite good. At its peak, its annual turnover reached over 1 million yuan. Even in recent years of poor market conditions, it has had an annual turnover of several hundred thousand yuan. It is a large-scale operation and can be considered a giant in the Southern City's iron industry. However, due to the increasingly poor market conditions, it has become impossible to operate. Yesterday, it engaged accountants Jiang Wanping and lawyer Jiang Ping to declare bankruptcy and liquidation. The Hengchangcheng Iron Works in Wuxi, which it also operates, has also declared bankruptcy. A meeting of Renji creditors will be held in Shanghai on October 12th, and a meeting of Hengchangcheng creditors will be held in Wuxi on October 19th.

Shenchangxiang Store

The Hengchangxiang general store, located at No. 10, Lane 300, Guangdong Road, has been in business for many years and has generally been thriving. However, due to the impact of poor market conditions, it has accumulated debt and become unable to maintain its operations. Yesterday, it engaged lawyer Hou Wan'an to announce liquidation and invite creditors to register their claims within ten days. Failure to do so will be considered a voluntary waiver of rights. All outstanding debts must also be paid in full within the specified period.

Yanruiji Store

Lawyer Jin Zhizhi, representing the Yanruiji Gu Store, announced liquidation and notified creditors to register their claims within 14 days. Failure to do so will be considered a voluntary waiver of rights.

Internationally Renowned Cultural Leader Nicholas Roerich Arrives in Shanghai - Roerich is an Artist, Writer, Antiquarian, and Philosopher Who Has Traveled Extensively in Central Asia and Mongolia in the Past Sixteen Months

Yulin Daily reports: Professor Nicholas Roerich, an internationally renowned artist, writer, antiquarian, and philosopher, and one of the recognized world cultural leaders, arrived in Shanghai on Monday from Beijing. Roerich was commissioned by the United States Department of Agriculture to collect drought-resistant grass seeds from Mongolia and Tibet. According to Roerich, if the grass seeds found in the deserts can be transplanted to the United States, farmers will not have to worry about their hard work being ruined by the climate. In the past sixteen months, Roerich has traveled extensively in Central Asia and Mongolia, collecting three to four hundred kinds of grass specimens, hoping to use them to prevent the drought that plagues the midwestern states of the United States. Roerich traveled to India on the President Monroe on Tuesday, planning to finish his unfinished work in the Himalayas and then return to New York. Roerich is also skilled in art. The Nicholas Roerich Museum in New York has thousands of his paintings, five hundred of which are related to Asia. The famous collector Anteliges once said, "Reading Roerich's paintings is like seeing a new world." Roerich has painted five hundred Himalayan mountain landscapes, which is truly commendable. Roerich has written many books on culture. His son, Dr. George Roerich, has traveled with him and has also written several books on Mongolia and Tibet. His recent work, a Tibetan-English dictionary, has not yet been published. During his stay in Shanghai, Roerich told a guest, "I am leaving China with the best feelings. I am very grateful for the kindness of the Chinese and Mongolian governments in helping me complete my cultural work." Roerich was born in 1874 in St. Petersburg, the former capital of Russia. He was both talented and eager to learn, so he enjoyed great fame in the world. After the Russian Revolution, he moved to the United States with his family in 1920.

Robbery During a Night Walk with a Dance Partner - One Robber Shot Dead by a Plainclothes Detective - Zhu Zhujin Joyfully Takes a Dance Partner Home After Dancing, Two Robbers Intercept and Rob, One Flees Far Away, One Shot Dead

Zhu Zhujin, a 26-year-old young man from Pudong, residing at No. 7, Yide Lane, Penglai Road, Nanshi, works at the Shanghai Inspectorate of the Ministry of Finance's Salt Affairs Bureau. Previously, he went to a dance hall on Jing'an Temple Road with his lover, Bu Nai Xin, a 22-year-old woman from Ningbo, to dance. At one o'clock yesterday morning, after enjoying themselves, the two left together to go home. Since the woman lived in the French Concession, Zhu walked with her to see her home, going from Xizang Road to the intersection of Songshan Road and Bo Pop Road in the French Concession. The two were walking and calling for rickshaws. As they walked in front of No. 414 Bo Pop Road, at exactly 1:30 AM, two robbers suddenly sprang out from the side of the road, one wearing a coffee-colored suit and the other a black gown, speaking in a local accent, and blocked their way. The robber in the suit showed a handgun and ordered Zhu and the woman to be quiet. The robber in the suit searched Zhu's suit pocket and took a five-yuan banknote from the Bank of China, one new silver dollar, and miscellaneous papers. The robber in the gown forcibly snatched a gold bracelet (worth 80 yuan) and a small rectangular chrome watch (worth 18 yuan) from Bu Nai Xin's hand. Zhu and the woman, seeing that the robbers had weapons, did not dare to resist and allowed them to search completely. The robbers ordered Zhu and the woman to return the way they came and not to look back. Zhu and the woman had no choice but to turn back and walk, and the robbers then strode away. Zhu and the woman walked for about three or five minutes and, knowing that the robbers had gone far, felt unwilling and turned back to chase after them, pursuing the shadows from about seven or eight zhang away. When they reached the intersection of Beile Road, they reported to the Chinese patrol officer No. 543 on duty there. The patrol officer immediately helped to pursue them and blew a whistle. The two robbers then scattered and fled. The robber in the suit turned north from Marang Road. As he approached Xiafei Road, Zhang Fengming, a plainclothes Chinese detective from Hebei from the Central Police Station, was heading home from work in a rickshaw. As he approached the intersection of Xiafei Road and Marang Road, he heard the noise, got out of the rickshaw, pulled out his handgun, and rushed to intercept them. Seeing the robber in the suit running towards him, Detective Zhang, holding his handgun, ordered him to stop. The robber, hearing the noise, immediately fired a shot to resist arrest. Detective Zhang dodged to the side and fired back, one bullet hitting the robber in the chest next to his right breast, and he fell to the ground. The robber fired another shot and then died, leaving behind a four-inch Browning handgun with five bullets still in the chamber. At this time, the victims and Chinese patrol officer No. 543 also arrived. Zhu recognized the robber who had robbed him. Detective Zhang immediately picked up the handgun and bullets and, with the help of rickshaw pullers Lu Afu (from Chongming) and Shi Sanrong (the bullet fired by the robber hit the shaft of his rickshaw), helped to carry the robber's body to the Xiafei Police Station and report the incident. The robber in the gown had already disappeared without a trace after the police station dispatched detectives to pursue him. The police chief ordered the robber's body to be taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for an autopsy. A wooden tag and a small knife were found on the body, as well as one yuan of the original stolen money. At 9:00 AM the next morning, Wang, the prosecutor from the Second Special Court, and Wei, the forensic doctor, and Peng, the clerk, arrived at the scene at noon to inspect the body. A bullet was extracted from the body. After the examination, they sat down to hear the case. Plainclothes detectives Zhang Quansheng and Zhang Fengming reported the incident and the investigation process in detail and presented the handgun, bullets, and confiscated items to the court. The victim, Wang Nai Xin, had not arrived, so Zhu Zhujin and the two rickshaw pullers, Lu and Shi, arrived to testify, describing the robbery and what they had witnessed. Zhu identified the silver dollar presented to the court as the stolen money. The official ordered the return of the silver dollar to Zhu and ruled that the unidentified man had died from a gunshot wound before his death. The body was handed over to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home to await identification by the family. The wooden tag and small knife were stored in the warehouse for collection. The handgun and five bullets were handed over to the detectives to investigate. The police department also ordered all detectives on duty to strictly investigate the fugitive robber and the stolen goods and bring them to justice.

He Xirui, Member of the Nanchang Air Force Team, Arrested in Shanghai - He is Originally from the Netherlands but is Considered to Have Lost His Citizenship - Nanchang Aviation Committee Believes He Xirui Has Engaged in Unlawful Conduct

He Xirui, a 24-year-old member of the Nanchang Air Force's 1st Team, whose father is named He Deru, is originally from the Netherlands. After graduating from aviation school in China, he served as a photographer and pilot in the Air Force's 1st Team. A month ago, He took leave to return to Xiamen, Fujian, to handle his father's funeral. After the funeral, he came to Shanghai, staying in Room 405 of the Cangzhou Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road. Recently, the Nanchang Aviation Committee, having received reports that He was impersonating a public official and engaging in other misconduct at the Cangzhou Hotel, sent a document to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau ordering an investigation. Chief Cai found that He was currently residing in Room 405 of the Cangzhou Hotel and sent detectives Su Gengsheng and Yuan Haisan to the First Special District Court to request an arrest warrant. Together with Tang Zihong, the chief of the Jing'an Temple Police Station, they secretly went to the hotel at about 10:00 AM the day before yesterday and arrested He, taking him to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they escorted him to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Special Court. Zhang Dayin, the police station's lawyer, stated that at 9:30 AM yesterday morning, a member of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau came to the police station with an arrest warrant from the court, requesting assistance in arresting He Xirui. However, after checking, He was found to be a Dutch citizen. Therefore, the police station was unsure whether the court's arrest warrant was valid for He and should first investigate with the Dutch Consulate whether He Xirui was registered there. Later, the Dutch Consul, Mr. Bell, verified the passport No. 9510 presented by He, proving that He was indeed a Dutch citizen. However, according to Mr. Bell's statement to the police station, according to Dutch law, any Dutch citizen who serves in another country without government permission is considered to have lost their citizenship. Since He had not obtained permission from the Dutch government, he should be considered to have lost his citizenship. The police station then went to the Cangzhou Hotel and arrested He. However, it is still unclear whether He's offense falls under criminal law or military law. A representative from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau told the police station that He had taken leave on July 9th of this year because someone in his family was ill and had not returned to work, which constituted desertion. However, the police station found a leave slip on He, with the leave period being from July 9th to October 9th, which seemed to be valid. According to the slip, the leave period had not yet expired. The representative requested instructions on how to proceed. Chen Guangyan, the captain of the Second Squad of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, stated that He Xirui had previously made a mistake in his work and was detained by the Nanchang Aviation Committee. Later, He was granted leave due to his father's death. Now, based on reports that He had abused his authority and spread rumors, he was arrested under orders from above. However, the details are unknown and must be requested from above. When questioned, He Xirui stated that he had been in Shanghai for a month and had been ill for more than half of that time. Last time, he was detained for seven days for breaking glass in the team while drunk. This time, he took leave because of his father's death and came to Shanghai, staying at the Cangzhou Hotel, and did not abuse his authority or spread rumors. He requested that evidence be presented. Judge Wu Zehan reviewed the confession and ordered He to be detained for further questioning on October 1st.

The United China Line's Mother You Steamer Will Sail Directly to Funing Tomorrow - A Distance of 300 Nautical Miles, Which Can Be Reached in 40 Hours, Stopping at Hexingzhen and Other Brands Along the Way

The China United Wharf & Warehouse Co. at 725 Wai Ma Road has opened a direct shipping route from Shanghai to Funing for the purpose of developing the planting industry in northern Jiangsu and facilitating commercial transport. The maiden voyage is scheduled for tomorrow. The Datong News Agency reporter has recorded the details as follows:

Abundant Production, Inconvenient Transportation

Funing is an important county town in northern Jiangsu, and its production of cotton, grains, and other products is extremely abundant. In addition, the production of livestock such as pigs, chickens, and ducks is also considerable. However, there has been no direct shipping route between Funing and Shanghai. Local products are transported by small inland vessels and private ships to ports such as Tongzhou and then loaded onto ships to Shanghai, which often takes more than ten days. The time wasted and the losses incurred are self-evident.

Successful Trial Voyage via the Sheyang River

The Shanghai United Wharf & Warehouse Co., recognizing that the existing route cannot reach Funing directly due to the danger of the entrance bar, which deters seagoing vessels from attempting it, sent Zhu Xinsheng, the head of the navigation department, on the Mother You Steamer to conduct a trial voyage via the Sheyang River on the 22nd of last month. It took only 40 hours to travel directly from Shanghai to Funing. The entire route is 300 nautical miles long.

Establishment of Offices in Important Ports

Yongxingji, 70 li from Funing, is also an important town. The Mother You Steamer sailed to that point at the time but stopped there because the water depth further upstream was less than 15 feet, making it difficult to navigate. The ship measured the route in detail and determined that it was possible to travel directly. Subsequently, offices were established in Sheyang River, Hexingzhen, Qianqiugang, Baojiadun, Wufangang, and Funing to facilitate stops along the way.

Official Direct Voyage to Funing Tomorrow

The company's Mother You Steamer has completed all the necessary arrangements along the route and is scheduled to officially sail to the newly opened Funing route tomorrow morning from Shanghai. The Datong News Agency reporter also learned that the Mother You Steamer is 230 feet long, 36 feet wide, has a draft of 8 feet when empty and 15 feet when fully loaded, has a capacity of 1,500 tons, and a speed of more than 10 nautical miles per hour. It is also learned that the captain of the ship is Shen Dafang and the first mate is Tang Beihang.

The International Trade Bureau Introduces Domestically Produced Goods

According to the International Trade Bureau yesterday, the bureau received several letters from abroad last week requesting domestically produced goods. They are listed below. It is hoped that manufacturers and exporters will request the bureau's guidance department to introduce them: (1) The Dutch Morley Iron Candy Biscuit Company intends to purchase various candies from China and requests instructions on everything. Goods can be financed by bank remittances. (2) The Dutch Almes Heiden City Wahlfu Jewelry Importer requests an introduction to jewelry, jade, gemstone, coral, and other jewelry manufacturers for trade. High-quality goods can be mailed, and payment will be made upon arrival. Commercial credit can be inquired at the Chinese Consulate in that city.

American Employee of Da Lai Steamship Company Commits Suicide by Shooting

Neither a Nervous Disorder Nor a Romantic Relationship, Only a Letter to Her Mother Saying She Could Not Cope With This World

The Greater America Evening News reports that Miss Dallas Brecht, an American employee of the Da Lai Steamship Company, committed suicide by shooting herself in the bathroom of her residence at No. 102, Lane 147, Hongqiao Road, this morning (the 24th). Her mother is currently on the President Jackson, coming to Shanghai from Seattle, and is expected to arrive next Tuesday. The deceased left a letter to her mother, only saying that she could no longer cope with this world, without explaining the reason for her suicide. Her friends are also unaware of the reason. The deceased was working in the company yesterday and seemed to be in good health. A friend spoke to her on the phone last night at 10:00 PM and did not hear her say anything pessimistic. It is reported that the deceased had dinner at home last night with a woman whose name is unknown. According to a mutual friend, the deceased had not been known to have any emotional turmoil. The deceased was 40 years old and had not yet married. Judging from the wording of her letter, there was no sign of a nervous disorder. Among her belongings, there was a promissory note for 1,000 yuan sent by her mother, dated June 25th, which had not yet been cashed. The deceased's mother is Canadian, and her father is German. Her mother lived in Shanghai for about 30 years and was very wealthy and well-known in Shanghai's social circles.

After the Yongfeng Electric Factory Closed Down, Shareholders Filed a Lawsuit Accusing the General Manager and Others of Colluding in Fraud and Embezzling More Than 10,000 Yuan of Company Funds

The Yongfeng Electric Manufacturing Factory, which has already closed down, was founded by Jiang Yinan and others as a joint venture, with Jiang serving as General Manager, Qi Zhou as Manager, Zhou Binghui as Engineer, and Jiang Hezhou (i.e., Jiang Chou) as Sales Director. Since starting operations in 1929, it failed after just six years. After the closure, shareholders Shen Weiqing, Zhao Kecheng, and Wu Zhuolun discovered that Jiang and others had colluded and engaged in fraudulent activities during their tenure, embezzling company funds totaling 100,241.288 yuan. They hired lawyer Wu Kaisheng to file a criminal self-accusation against Jiang and Zhou for embezzlement and breach of trust. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yu Gui of the First Special District District Court held a hearing. None of the four defendants appeared in court. Lawyers Yan Gang and Yan Qisheng appeared on their behalf and requested a postponement, citing that the defendants were mostly out of Shanghai on business and that the case involved complex Japanese matters, hindering them from preparing their defense. The court then questioned the plaintiff, Wu Zhuolun, about the basis of the lawsuit. Wu stated that the company had thirteen shareholders with a total of 296 shares. The three of them had each invested 500 yuan. The factory was located in Hongxing Lane on Beijing Road, specializing in the manufacture of flashlights. There was a partnership agreement in place at the time, but the defendants violated the terms of the agreement in all their actions during their tenure. It has now been discovered that the company's funds have been embezzled to the huge sum of over 100,000 yuan, and the defendants have not left Shanghai, but are actually avoiding appearing in court. Judge Liu therefore adjourned the hearing, pending the arrival of the defendants for further questioning.

Zheng Wencai Privately Sells Red Pills and Attempts to Frame Others, Sentenced to Six Months in Prison

Zheng Wencai, from Qingjiang, has recently been selling red pills in the Pu'ai Alley near Zhoujia Bridge for profit. The day before yesterday at noon, he suddenly reported to the Yangshupu Police Station, claiming that he knew this kind of livelihood was against the law but was forced to do it by circumstances. He claimed the main perpetrator was Wang Xiaofeng, a fellow townsman, and his accomplice was Liu Wanning. He said the women who handed over the red pills were Ms. Wu, Ms. Guo, and Ms. Zhu, who could sell more than 500 pills a day and give him small change for food. Now, disregarding the consequences, he had revealed their business to Wang, but Wang refused to let him quit and threatened to kill him with an axe, so he made a special trip to turn himself in. He then produced a package of evidence, 120 poisonous pills. The police chief dispatched detective Zi Shouqi, who arrested Wang, Liu, and the three women at 40 Songpan Road, and took them into custody. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Lawyer Li Zhishan of the Bureau of Public Works stated the circumstances and claimed that the defendants denied the charges at the police station. When Zheng Wencai, listed as the first defendant, gave his testimony, it was the same as what he had said at the police station. When Wang was questioned, he claimed to have known Zheng for years but had only borrowed a few silver dollars from him. He accused Zheng of making false accusations and asked the court to examine the red pills, claiming they were his own. He hired lawyer Yan Gang to defend him. Liu Wan wrote a statement similar to Wang's. Ms. Wang and the other two women stated that they never sold red pills. Judge Xiao Bianfen sentenced Zheng Wencai to six months in prison, the red pills were confiscated, and the other five defendants, including Wang Xiaofeng, were found not guilty. Lawyer Li dropped the appeal and released them.

Vegetable Stalls on Kangti Road Petitioned to Party and Government Agencies Yesterday, All 83 Households, Hundreds of Old and Young, Are Living in Extreme Panic, Demanding an Early Solution

The vegetable stalls on Kangti Road in the French Concession of this city were ordered by the police to temporarily relocate to Rue du Père Huc in February this year due to road construction in the area. However, on September 7th, they were suddenly evicted by the police. The stalls immediately moved back to Kangti Road but were still evicted, making it impossible for them to operate. Nine representatives were immediately elected to submit petitions to the French Police Station, the Taxpayers' Association, etc., requesting the maintenance of the stalls. At the same time, the stores on Kangti Road jointly sent letters to the French Consul-General, the French Municipal Council, and the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession, asking them to uphold justice and maintain the livelihoods of the stallholders, which were all on file. However, more than ten days have passed without a solution. All 83 households of vegetable stall vendors, hundreds of old and young, are living in extreme panic. In order to seek an early solution, all the stallholders marched to the City Party Headquarters at around 9:00 AM yesterday to petition. Mr. Zhu Yangwu received them. Representatives Sun Chuanfu and Wang Fusheng stated the circumstances of setting up the stalls, the situation of being banned by the French police, and demanded the maintenance of their livelihoods. Mr. Zhu replied that he would immediately consult the municipal government for negotiation. The representatives then left and relayed the information to the stallholders, who were all satisfied and dispersed. At 2:00 PM, representatives Sun Chuanfu, Wang Fusheng, Li Fugen, Zhou Wenxian, and Ye Shuiwang took the petition to the Municipal Government Central District to petition the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau. They first went to the Social Affairs Bureau, where they were received by Mr. Wang Zhusun, who promised to send someone to investigate and handle the matter. The representatives then left and made the same petition to the municipal government, which promised to handle the matter. The representatives were satisfied and dispersed.

Inspection Report of Zhejiang Local Bank

The 71st inspection report of the Zhejiang Local Bank Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee states that the committee members and commissioned accountants conducted the 71st inspection at the bank on September 20, 1935. The inspection results are listed as follows: Total amount of exchange notes issued: 3,286,280.50 yuan, including silver dollar notes: 2,834,585.70 yuan, and fractional currency notes: 451,694.80 yuan. Total amount of exchange note reserves: 3,286,280.50 yuan, including cash reserve in silver dollars: 2,342,120.05 yuan, and collateral reserve converted into silver dollars: 944,160.00 yuan. According to Article 2 of the Zhejiang Local Bank Exchange Note Regulations, 60% of the issued exchange notes should be cash reserve and 40% should be collateral reserve. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve is above 70% and the collateral reserve is below 30%, which is in line with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. Special Item

Concerning Suggestions on Increasing Negotiable Instruments (4)

5. Deficiencies in the Financial System

Although the loss of negotiable instruments used for payment is substantial, it has not yet reached a state of depletion, as mentioned above. However, why is it that the payment of negotiable instruments has not been depleted, while financial turnover has become extremely difficult? This must be further attributed to the deficiencies in the financial system. In Shanghai over the past decade or so, the old financial system has gradually collapsed, while a new financial system has not yet been established. The dynamics of financial circulation are merely a disorderly, unplanned pouring-in, rather than a systematic cycle. In normal times, when credit is loose, investments and loans are made independently, each acting on its own, which easily leads to excessive credit expansion. Once a crisis suddenly arises, everyone panics, tightening credit severely, resulting in an unwarranted credit crunch. In the current situation, if the financial industry could provide its strength, market panic could be alleviated almost overnight. However, the financial industry's inability to do so readily has its own difficulties. Namely, after the financial industry extends credit to industry and commerce, who can then extend credit to the financial industry? If there is no backing, the financial industry's own lack of funds would not be a blessing for the country. To solve these two problems, we must actively improve the financial organization, creating a great financial center force to serve as the backing for the financial industry and the hub for financial turnover, so that the financial organization itself can first achieve systematic circulation. Passively, we must also prevent the currency in this circulation from flowing out in large quantities due to the inability to balance international payments. Only in this way can the financial industry complete its organic circulation and fulfill its due role in the national economic system. However, to achieve this goal, the full utilization of credit instruments is essential. Details will be discussed below.

6. Modern Credit Instruments

As mentioned above, the improper use of credit instruments is the biggest deficiency in the current financial system. Payment instruments are like power, while credit instruments are like machinery. Without power, machinery cannot operate, but without sufficient machinery, power is wasted without benefiting production. Therefore, if the use of credit instruments is not vigorously promoted, even if we import foreign capital or even inflate the currency, the result will only fuel speculation and abnormal economic development.

The main credit instruments in modern financial markets are twofold: one is industrial securities, including stocks and corporate bonds; the other is negotiable instruments, typically bank acceptances and commercial acceptances. The issuance and trading of industrial securities create a long-term capital market in the financial system, with the stock exchange as its representative institution. Industrial and commercial enterprises use this to obtain capital, and the general public uses this to invest in industry, leading to the rise of large-scale production enterprises under corporate organization, and thus the development of the national economy. The acceptance and discounting of negotiable instruments create a short-term capital market in the financial system, which can be analyzed as an acceptance market and a discount market. The former involves banks accepting collateral or guarantees provided by industrial and commercial enterprises and accepting the long-term drafts they issue, which are bank acceptances. These instruments are traded publicly in the market, with a publicly determined market price, forming the acceptance market. The latter involves industrial and commercial enterprises selling goods on credit and then issuing long-term drafts, which are accepted by the debtors who purchased the goods on credit, forming commercial acceptances. These instruments are financed by the financial industry through discounting, with the financial industry determining a public discount rate and discounting accordingly, forming the discount market. Through the use of the acceptance market and the discount market, industry and commerce can obtain short-term financing.

A financial system must have a long-term capital market and a short-term capital market to be considered sound. The long-term capital market must use stocks and corporate bonds as the main instruments, and the short-term capital market must use bank acceptances and commercial acceptances as the main instruments to be considered equipped with the necessary conditions for a modern financial market. (To be continued)

Guangxi Swimming Athletes - Participating in the National Games - Flag-Giving Ceremony Held in Nanning - Bai Chongxi Delivers Training Speech to Athletes

(Nanning Correspondence) Guangxi Province has previously not sent athletes to participate in the National Games due to various reasons. The 6th National Games of the Double Tenth Festival will be held in Shanghai this year. The sports community of the province believes that track and field, ball games, and martial arts are not yet fully trained, and therefore cannot send representatives to attend immediately. Only swimming is well-trained, so it has been decided this year to send swimming athletes to participate. The Guangxi Swimming Athletes Group has been established and trained for several months. The best performers are Huang Jinghuan and Su Fangneng in the 100-meter and 50-meter freestyle, respectively. Huang Jinghuan and Lei Bing are also the best in the 400-meter and 2,500-meter freestyle. Liu Kun in the men's 300-meter breaststroke and Xu Zhenwan in the women's 200-meter are both outstanding individuals. In addition, men's and women's relay swimming also have hopes of competing in the National Games. The Guangxi authorities, in order to encourage the young athletes, held a flag-giving ceremony in Nanning on the 15th of this month, as the Guangxi swimming athletes are participating in the National Games for the first time this year. The venue was the Nanning Lequn Society. Military and political figures all attended the ceremony, including Bai Chongxi, Huang Xuchu, Li Pinxian, Wang Zanbin, Liang Hansong, Qiu Changwei, Lei Peihong, and hundreds of representatives from various agencies and organizations. The meeting was announced to begin at noon, chaired by Li Pinxian, who gave the opening speech, stating that the swimming athletes of the province are about to go to Shanghai to attend the National Games, marking the first time the province's sports banner will be displayed in the National Games. He hoped that the athletes would take it a step further, practice continuously, and strive to win the reputation of Guangxi youth sports in the National Games. Next, Bai Chongxi delivered a training speech to the athletes, stating that this is the first time Guangxi has sent athletes to participate in the National Games. The significance of sports lies in strengthening the physique and revitalizing the national spirit. In the past, the province implemented military training throughout the province, which was also intended to prepare for national salvation. Since China promoted sports, it has previously focused on trophyism, cultivating a small number of athletes, and ball games such as tennis belong to the aristocracy. Therefore, the province has decided on three principles for promoting sports: first, to be universal; second, to be economical and easy to implement; and third, to be practical. All 13 million people in the province should have the opportunity to participate in sports, and the focus should be on economical and practical items, so special attention is paid to swimming, mountain climbing, track and field, and shooting, with the aim of strengthening the physique to bear the responsibility of saving the country and the nation. This time, it is gratifying to win the National Games, but it is not shameful to lose. I hope that you will show the spirit of "hard work and endurance," "sincerity and bravery," and "hard work and hardship" of the Guangxi people at any time and in any place. All aspects of life should be disciplined and implement the province's sports aims. After the speech, the flag-giving ceremony was held. The athletes gathered on the commander's ship and nominated representative Lei Bingchang to step forward to pay respects to the chairman. The chairman returned the salute and presented a yellow flag to the athletes' representative. The ceremony was solemn, and the representative returned the salute as required before retreating. At this time, military music was played, and the ceremony was completed. The athletes then held an aquatic sports meet at the society's swimming pool, and also took the opportunity to select external athletes to avoid missing any talent, including Bai Bingjian and Li Dazhi in the men's 50-meter freestyle, Huang Zhicheng in the 1,500-meter, and Lei Xiufen, Lei Mujie, and Pang Baohua in the women's 50-meter freestyle. This City's Guangdong Swimming Team Raises Questions About the Swimming Preliminary Selection

——Requests Remediation from the Preliminary Selection Committee——

Wen Jingling and Xu Heng Were Not Selected

Requests Foreign Judges for Diving Preliminary Selection

This city's Guangdong Swimming Team has raised questions about the swimming preliminary selection for the National Games. It is reported that the team entrusted Peng Sanmei to manage everything for this city's National Games swimming preliminary selection, and the team has always been enthusiastic and supportive, deeply congratulating the swimming community of Shanghai on obtaining such a capable person. However, from the start of training to the end of the selection, the process has deviated from the principles of preliminary selection and caused dissatisfaction among the team members. In order to maintain the team members' sportsmanship, the team has sent letters to the Municipal Government and the Shanghai National Games Preliminary Selection Committee requesting remediation, and now lists the inappropriate points below:

According to the selection of the swimming team, it is divided into speed and diving. The selection method for the former is free registration, regular practice, and testing of each member's results as the selection standard, which is excellent and fair. However, team member Wen Jingling's exquisite swimming skills have always been famous. For example, when representing China at the Shanghai International Swimming Competition recently, he also performed excellently in front of the entire city's population. This time, his failure to be selected was unexpected. After investigation, the team feels regret that the results of some of the representatives selected are far inferior to Wen's. Some say that the reason Wen was not selected was because he could not attend practice every day. It is unknown that Wen is studying at Shanghai University, and it is difficult to travel back and forth every day. This had been notified to the host in advance, because studies should not be neglected, and the daily travel expenses are quite a lot (about three or four yuan), which is difficult for a student to bear. Also, he can still practice normally at the school. Therefore, for the sake of Shanghai's sports, and to encourage studious athletes, it seems necessary to remedy this regrettable event. Team member Xu Heng represented the city at the last National Games, and one of the most valuable points Shanghai obtained in swimming was due to this gentleman's strength, so as not to get a goose egg. His usual results show that the short-distance 50 meters is often under 30 seconds. When he participated in the three-style relay performance at the opening of the new city pool, his speed in the third leg certainly surpassed the others, and was better than the selected representative Zhang Rongguang. At that time, Zhang won the second leg of the frog-style, and after winning, he entered the water before Xu, but when he reached the finish line, he was equal to Xu. This is a fact that everyone saw, and there is no need to say more. As for those who blame Xu for not participating in training and should not be selected, it is even more incomprehensible. The preliminary selection had long stated that it would also look at usual performance as a standard for selection, and Xu has always been an excellent swimmer, but he was not able to participate in training because he had not returned from Java. Moreover, the representative selected last time had priority to attend. For example, Liang Peiyu of this year's women's tennis team was promoted to captain because she was sick and did not participate in the preliminary selection. This can be cited. Also, after the end of this preliminary selection, Peng repeatedly emphasized in the recent public competition of the Municipal Government that if the 500-meter racers achieved a result within 34 minutes, they could be rewarded with the opportunity to participate in the National Games as a representative. However, at the opening day of the city pool, he lightly let go of the well-known short-distance athletes like Xu Heng, and did not let them have a chance to try. This is really incomprehensible.

As for the diving group selection, it ended on the evening of the 16th at the West Youth Pool. This selection was not fully prepared in advance and was presided over by Peng alone. The results of the judging were especially regrettable.

Upon investigation, the judges for this competition were not announced in advance. Peng temporarily invited Mr. Bright of West Youth to serve as the judge. The authorities handled this important matter so hastily. How can the certainty of the criticism be determined? It can be imagined.

As for the style of fancy diving, the judges' criticisms vary from person to person, and each has their own subjective views. For the same posture, some find a magnificent body beautiful, while others find a short and lean body aesthetically pleasing. Therefore, diving competitions in various countries around the world mostly have more than three judges to gather opinions from several parties for a fair judgment. Moreover, the position of the judges and the evaluation of the merits of the diver's posture are also greatly related. Only one judge was set up this time, how can the whole picture be seen? This has already lost the meaning of judging.

Upon investigation, the representatives selected by China in recent years have all been filled by Chinese people as judges. However, Peng this time favored foreigners, and the intention is unknown. However, language barriers and conflicting meanings have already had a great impact on the athletes' results.

Sincerely, one hundred and fifty members of the Shanghai Guangdong Swimming Team.

Ministry of Education Revises Reporting Matters for Educational Administrative Organs

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the Education Bureaus of all provinces and cities on the 23rd, stating that in order to standardize the reporting matters of the educational administrative organs of all provinces and cities for comparison, it issued Instruction No. 1910 in December of the 18th year (of the Republic) promulgating a schedule of periodic reporting matters for the educational administrative organs of all provinces and cities. Most educational administrative organs in the provinces and cities have been able to follow the instructions and report on schedule. However, since many years have passed, some of the items listed in the original schedule are no longer applicable. Therefore, the Ministry has revised the schedule and is issuing it as an attachment. All provinces and cities are instructed to comply with it without delay or omission. This is of utmost importance. This order.

Revised Schedule of Periodic Reporting Matters for Educational Administrative Organs of Provinces and Cities:

Administrative plans of provincial and municipal educational administrative organs: Report once within one month before the start of each academic year.

Work reports of provincial and municipal educational administrative organs: Compiled and reported once at the end of March, June, September, and December each year.

Inspection reports of supervisors of provincial and municipal educational administrative organs: Summarized and reported once within one month after the end of each year.

Information on the academic qualifications, experience, positions, and salaries of senior officials of provincial and municipal educational administrative organs: Reported once at the end of June and December each year.

Number and vacancies of government-funded students studying abroad and scholarship students: Reported once at the end of December each year.

Academic qualifications, experience, and salaries of county and city education bureau chiefs or section chiefs in charge of education in county governments: Compiled and reported once at the end of June each year.

Academic qualifications, experience, and salaries of directors of social education institutions: Compiled and reported once each year.

Overview of mass schools and various supplementary schools, and reporting of the number of new and graduating students each semester.

Overview of literacy campaigns: Reported once every June.

Establishment and progress of education halls, museums, art galleries, libraries, reading rooms, and public sports fields: Reported once at the end of June each year.

Progress of compulsory education: Reported once at the end of June each year.

Various forms and registers stipulated in the amended regulations for middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools shall be reported periodically in accordance with the provisions of the respective regulations.

Items listed in Article 20 of the amended regulations for private schools shall be forwarded within one month after the end of each academic year.

Educational facilities for Mongolians, Tibetans, Muslims, and Miao people in border provinces: Reported once at the end of June each year.

Liu Haisu's Opinions on Improving the Art School System

Liu Haisu, the president of the Art Academy, believes that the current art school system in our country is not perfect. In particular, the fixed study period of three years is too short, and the admission qualification limited to high school graduates presents many difficulties. He has sent a letter to Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education outlining his opinions on improvement. The original letter is transcribed below:

Respectfully, last month, I, Haisu, went to Beijing and discussed with the Minister the improvement of the art academy system in our country. I was deemed important and asked to draft a plan. Haisu, considering this a major matter, returned to Shanghai and conducted thorough discussions with various parties, and the principles have been tentatively determined. My humble opinions are presented as follows: (1) Improvement of the education system. Article 5 of the revised regulations for specialized schools states that art schools are classified as Type D specialized schools, with a study period of two years, similar to vocational schools for industry, agriculture, and commerce. The admission qualification requires graduation from senior high school, similar to the admission level of various departments of universities. In Europe, art schools and music schools, whose purpose is to train senior art experts and music experts, have no fixed admission qualifications, but require strict examinations, especially considering whether they have talent. Graduation also has a fixed time limit, and their research process is similar to that of universities, so they are often called research institutes or academies. According to Haisu's observation and experience, art schools and music schools in various countries are fundamentally different from other vocational schools. It is not reasonable to list them alongside other vocational specialized schools. A three-year study period is too short, and requiring a high school diploma for admission is inappropriate. The study of art and music mostly requires talent. Throughout history, many immortal writers, in terms of their level of general education, may not be equivalent to today's high school graduates, and there are not a few on the art history who failed because they were alienated from subjects that did not suit their temperament. The development of artistic temperament is the most important thing, and those with artistic talent often have a dislike for mechanical subjects. If they are forced to study them, it will not only not help their studies, but also harm the growth of their talent. If one cannot graduate from high school, there is no way to advance in school. Graduates also find that high school courses focus on subjects such as mathematics, physics, and chemistry, and artistic subjects are often omitted. In this way, after two years, the opportunity is gone, the age is long, and the hand is stiff and the eye is dull, and it is difficult to achieve anything. Although our country is currently in a transitional era and does not need to be perfect in everything, the distinction between advanced learning and general technology must be clarified. In the field of art schools and music schools, whether it is training teachers or experts, it cannot be equated with general vocational skills and classified as specialized schools. It should be renamed the Academy of Fine Arts or the Academy of Music. For the sake of meeting the urgent needs of society, such as the training of teachers of music, art, and handicrafts, it may be considered the same as vocational skills for the sake of quick success, but advanced learning must be treated as a separate matter and cannot be mixed. In Haisu's humble opinion, art schools and music schools should admit junior high school graduates, with a fixed study period of five years, the last three years for specialized subjects, and the first year for preparatory subjects. The departments for training teachers may be shortened slightly, which is already a compromise compared to European countries. Whether students study pure art, applied art, or teacher training, they must undergo strict basic training in the first two years of preparatory subjects. Students who do not meet the required level should be required to take compulsory remedial courses. Only when they reach perfection can they advance to the next level. If we believe that advanced learning cannot be borrowed, and if we want scholars to avoid superficial words, then the improvement of the education system is a matter that cannot be delayed. (2) Principles of improvement. A. Elevating pure art. Before the advent of modern technology, there were great artists and thinkers who, with a spirit of perseverance, engaged in ideological and artistic movements to inspire the national character of excellence and perseverance and to stir up a spirit of enterprise. Great artists are the soul of a nation, enduring for thousands of years. All countries devote their efforts to artistic construction and dare not lag behind. Great artists are especially admired. At this time of national rejuvenation in our country, artistic talents should be encouraged and supported in the hope of expressing the ideology of this great era and building our new Chinese national culture. Therefore, the pure art departments of art schools, such as students studying painting and sculpture, should have their level specially raised, and their academic year should be at least five years, or even not stipulated, and they can graduate only after their usual performance is approved by the school council. In ordinary times, special attention should be paid to the cultivation of their character and the training of their thoughts. The content of the course should be simple, appropriate, profound, and the preparatory subjects should be as complete as possible. B. Developing applied art. At present, China is an economically backward country with a trade deficit. The promotion of applied art is extremely urgent. The critic Ruskin often sought out the thoughts, feelings, and moral spirit of each era from architecture and applied art. The manifesto of the Constructivist faction even contains the phrase "Anything that cannot be practical cannot be called art." This shows that it occupies an extremely prominent position culturally and economically. According to the current needs of China, art schools should urgently establish a department of applied art to train production talents in applied art and use new European methods to improve and promote China's inherent handicrafts such as metal casting, ceramics, embroidery, and weaving, so as to meet the requirements of the times. This is also an important issue that should be decided first in the improvement of the education system.

Central Party Headquarters Orders Local Party Headquarters to Dismiss Scout Instructors, Directly Managed by Local Councils

The Boy Scouts in our country were originally managed and guided by personnel jointly dispatched by local party and government departments. Now, the Central Party Headquarters has formally established the Boy Scout General Association, and all Boy Scout affairs in various places are directly managed by the association. All Boy Scout instructors have been dismissed. The original text of the Central Command to local party headquarters is recorded below: (Omitted above) It has been found that the Boy Scout profession in our country has been largely guided and carried out by personnel dispatched by local party headquarters and education departments in the past. Now that the Boy Scout General Association of China has been formally established, all Boy Scout affairs in various places should be unified under the management of the association in order to unify authority. According to the association's request, all Boy Scout instructors in provinces and cities where Boy Scout councils or councils' preparatory offices have been formally established shall be dismissed, and their affairs shall be directly managed by the local councils or councils' preparatory offices, so as to assign responsibilities. The 186th standing committee meeting of the association has decided to approve the case. In addition to distribution, this order is hereby issued for compliance.

Chinese Ambassador to Germany, Cheng Tianfang, Lectures at Tongji University

At 11:00 AM on the 23rd of this month, Cheng Tianfang, the first Chinese Ambassador to Germany, visited the National Tongji University in Wusong to attend the school's memorial week lecture. All Chinese and German faculty and students of the school attended, and the occasion was very grand. The school president, Weng Zhilong, first gave an introduction, stating that Ambassador Cheng is an advanced member of the party and the country, a leader of the cultural movement, and is now honored to be the first ambassador to Germany, and will certainly promote Sino-German relations and cultural cooperation. Ambassador Cheng then gave a lecture, first stating that he is willing to work hard to promote Sino-German relations and culture, and then said that China's crisis is that externally, it is oppressed by strong neighbors and is situated between two major powers, and the national situation is in danger. Internally, due to the import surplus of foreign trade, economic bankruptcy has been formed, coupled with natural disasters and man-made disasters, and it is sufficient to destroy the country without foreign aggression. The responsibility for saving the country lies in the general knowledge and youth who have received higher education, and they must work hard for the country. The past of merely shouting slogans and running around, and the recent depression and disappointment, are not the ways to save the country. We must cultivate strength and the determination to serve the country, and then express it with appropriate methods. Some people may think that the foreign insults suffered by China are all due to the weakness of the navy, army, and air force, but they do not know that the strength of a country's navy, army, and air force depends entirely on the degree of progress in industries, economy, education, and science. Therefore, the efforts of young people in libraries and research rooms are of the same value as soldiers fighting on the battlefield. The medical and engineering departments of Tongji University are the two departments most needed for the revival of the Chinese nation, because they will not only treat individual diseases, but their major task is to promote the health of the nation, extend the years of national service, and enhance the spirit and courage to take on responsibilities. Engineering can directly promote the development of domestic industry and science, indirectly assist the progress of the navy, army, and air force, and can eliminate natural disasters, relieve the people's difficulties, and revitalize transportation. It can not only facilitate the transportation of agricultural products and develop the national economy, but also make political exchanges more frequent and easier to unite. This is why industry is even more important. Finally, he also said that the revival of Germany is mostly due to the hard-working and patient spirit of the intellectual class and university professors, as an encouragement to the audience, who were all moved and changed their expressions.

Little Boy (Five or Six)

— Original by American Miss Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

Poor old Huanghua has been in a bad mood these days because she recently lost her calf and is very sad. Therefore, she sees all human beings as her enemies (who can blame her)? So when that "Matador" (Note 1) leaped towards her, with a red handkerchief hanging from the tip of his spear and flying in the wind, she only raised her head and mooed! Taomi still rode towards her, but seeing it was his old friend, he was willing to get closer, but when the spear hit her back and made a bang, both the donkey and the cow were taken aback and felt disgusted. Taobi took a step back and neighed to express his sympathetic protest, and the old Huanghua cow, after this blow, lowered her horns and was filled with hatred.

(Note 1) Matador is a person who fights bulls in Spain. If the bull loses, he will slaughter the bull.

"Hit her again, don't let her go, Taomo; she's angry and will be here soon!" Tang En shouted, and he rushed up from behind with another stick, and Jieke and Neda did the same.

Old Huanghua saw that she was surrounded and treated impolitely, so she walked quickly around the field, feeling worse every moment. Later, she became mad, because no matter which direction she walked, there was always a terrible child shouting wildly and waving a strange and hateful whip. They thought it was very interesting! But it was really painful for her, until she couldn't bear it any longer, and suddenly changed the whole situation with a swift and violent move. She suddenly turned around and rushed straight to her old friend Taobi, because she really hated him for pushing her too hard. Poor Taobi, who was slow to move, quickly retreated backwards, but lost his balance when he was tripped by a stone. Poor man, horse, and everything fell into a chaotic mess. Old Huanghua, in a panic, jumped over the wall and ran wildly along the road.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Wang Yu)

When taking things to pawn, one hopes that the amount of money on the pawn ticket is large; when redeeming, one hopes that the amount of money on the pawn ticket is small.

Many people in Shanghai change their clothes for the four seasons in pawnshops.

A pawn ticket that has expired, I don't know how many tears it has been stained with.

Things pawned in the pawnshop are like a person committing a crime and going to jail; after eighteen months, it's like being in jail and still being shot in the end.

Pawnshops were originally for emergency relief, but often a person dies more quickly from being in urgent need because all his things have been pawned.

These days, pawnshops are "stopping pawning and waiting for redemption," ordinary people are "stopping redemption and only pawning," and the poor are "unable to pawn and unable to redeem."

Only the rich are qualified to open pawnshops, and the counters of pawnshops are all very high, which is to tell us that the poor are "too high to reach."

Vitamin X

— Zhu Ying

Let's hold back on boasting about the progress of modern science and the brilliance of medicine. X-rays, radium, vitamins A, B, C, D, and everything else seem capable of bringing life back to any difficult or complex illness. But in reality, for all the prevalent mental illnesses today, what remedy is there other than watching patients choose to take "sleeping pills," "Lysol," "raw opium," and other such passive treatments?

The mental illnesses I'm talking about, listen, are not those that can be treated in mental asylums, nor are they illnesses that Chinese and foreign doctors can diagnose through observation, auscultation, questioning, and palpation. Naturally, they are even less curable by bottled, boxed, or packaged pills, powders, or liquids. The only symptom of this kind of mental illness is sighing and lamenting, with everything confined to extreme negativity and pessimism. The sources of the illness can be divided into two types: failure in love and failure in career or difficulties in life.

The only miraculous cure for this type of mental illness, to put it bluntly, is known to everyone except fools: shining silver dollars. But "shining silver dollars" is not a suitable name for a medicine, so it is named "Vitamin X." For example, for those who have failed in love, as long as they are given "Vitamin X," they won't have to worry about not conquering the other party. Those who have failed in their careers, after taking Vitamin X, will it not be the same as taking a stimulant? Do they still need to worry about not being able to rise up again?

However, although I have this great invention that benefits the masses, because the cost of this elixir is too high, I cannot start to formulate it. But at the same time, I dare not keep it secret, so I am publishing it specifically, perhaps there are many wealthy philanthropists in the world who will donate to help the world.

Please note that at present, in the areas of the Yellow River and Yangtze River floods, a large amount of Vitamin X is urgently needed!

The Problem of Getting on the Bus

— Yang Yusheng

On Nanjing Road on Sundays, you can encounter Westerners and their wives everywhere. They are most polite to white women, and everywhere they are practicing the principle of "Ladies first," but it is not like this for Chinese women. It seems that Chinese people should not receive this kind of politeness from white people, which is really enough to make people feel disheartened.

However, Chinese men are now also striving to "respect" women and are practicing the principle of "Ladies first" everywhere. Although Chinese women cannot avoid the contempt of white men, they can still receive the "tenderness" of their own men. They can still be considered fortunate!

The day before yesterday, while waiting for a public bus in the crowd near the New World, a small dispute arose between a Chinese "Westernized" couple and a "foreign" couple because they were scrambling to get on the bus. The Chinese man, wanting to show Western politeness, was about to "support" his woman onto the bus when he was suddenly stopped by an arm with a hand covered in yellow hair. At the same time, he heard the phrase "Ladies first" in a foreign accent. He was embarrassed to disobey the foreign man who was observing this principle! The foreign woman took advantage of this opportunity and got on the bus. The foreign man also wanted to get on the bus, but he was stopped by an arm with a hand covered in exposed blue veins. He also heard the phrase "Ladies first" in English. He seemed surprised that a Chinese person dared to mess with him, but he saw that to the left of the Chinese man stood his wife, who was eager to get on the bus. So he felt that the meaning of the word "Ladies" should not be divided by race! Helplessly, he retracted the foot he had placed on the bus!

I wish I could know that man's name now, because he was able to win back some face for our Chinese women!

Uneven Distribution of Booty!

— Shi Ying

The Piao Miao Records of Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

When eating, the imperial kitchen first presented her with a small silver hot pot; because chrysanthemums were always in season in the autumn, hot pot had quickly become a necessity at banquets. Although it seemed a bit early, it was not surprising. What was noteworthy was the relationship between the chrysanthemums and the hot pot. Originally, the hot pot was already filled with more than half a pot of original chicken broth or meat broth. The lid was made very tightly, so that the temperature would not easily dissipate, and even the fresh and fragrant smell would not escape. At this time, the chief eunuch in charge of meals, Zhang Dean, had already prepared a small dining table slightly larger than a tea table in front of the Empress Dowager's seat. There was a round hole in the center of this table, which could just stably support the hot pot in the middle; originally, this table was designed specifically for this purpose. Along with the hot pot, several shallow small plates were brought out from the imperial kitchen, filled with thinly sliced raw fish or raw chicken slices that had been skinned and boned; but because the Empress Dowager liked to eat fish, sometimes only fish slices were prepared, with a little sauce and vinegar.

The washed chrysanthemum petals were naturally also piled on this small table. Then Zhang Dean reached out and lifted the lid of the hot pot, but did not put it down, only holding it in his hand to wait. The Empress Dowager personally picked up a few slices of fish or meat and put them into the soup, and Zhang Dean quickly replaced the lid. At this time, the person eating—the Empress Dowager herself—and the people watching—our group—all solemnly and quietly waited, with dozens of gazes focused on the hot pot. (424)

Suffering by Association

— (Er Yu)

Chinese people, no matter what they do, have a tendency to not seek thorough understanding, which is perhaps why careers stagnate and do not advance. Taking reading as an example, today's students are most fond of showing off their cleverness, finishing a very thick book in just half a day. Whether they can have a deep and accurate understanding is something no one can control. I will give an extremely simple example: "suffering by association." Most people explain it as disaster befalling the fish in the pond. In fact, a "shen" character is missing between "chi" (pond) and "yu" (fish). "Chi Zhongyu" was a scholar of the Chu state whose house was burned down by a neighbor's fire, so the phrase "suffering by association" came about. Now many people use it in articles, but its origin has long been lost.

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: Senior Officials Cherish Their Reputation and Know How to Knock on Doors; New Love Departs From Flesh and Blood, With No Way to Visit the Sick

Still halfway up the stairs, not yet upstairs, he took out a handkerchief from his pocket, wiping his sweat as he nodded to Ze Cheng and smiled: "I finally completed the mission." County Magistrate Zhou is still waiting for me to discuss other matters, so I won't go upstairs. Please reply to Commissioner Lan. After saying this, he turned around and went downstairs. He walked back to his room, passing the entrance of Gan Zhiqian, and saw that he was still reading under the light, so he said to himself: "I knew Commissioner Lan would have to ask me for help! I'm not bragging." Although he was talking to himself, his voice was still not very low. This caused the servant to immediately come in and pour him water and make tea. Following this, Qiu Ze Cheng also came to visit, asking him about the outcome of the negotiations. Jie Fu boasted for a while, saying that everything had been smoothed over. However, there was one matter that he had asked Mr. Jia to introduce, but now Mr. Jia was a little unhappy and unwilling to write a letter of introduction again, so he had made a considerable sacrifice for Commissioner Lan. As he said this, he kept frowning and sighing. Ze Cheng sat in silence for a while. Seeing that his expression was somewhat unhappy, he pondered and said: "I don't know whether the commissioner can introduce talent as soon as he arrives here. But perhaps I can help in other places." Jie Fu immediately smiled and said: "I am not a big figure, so I won't talk about developing the Northwest. As long as I have food to eat, I can go to any place." Hearing this, Ze Cheng could not help but smile a little. Jie Fu immediately straightened his face and said: "Although I cannot avoid asking Commissioner Lan for help, I definitely do not have any intention of coercing him. Even if he doesn't come up with a solution for me, I will still be a mediator to the end. Didn't I say so? I remember that we are still from the same hometown." (324)

Local Customs and Scenery

The Spectacle of Japanese Cafés

— Ji Yun

Drinking coffee was originally a habit of Europeans and Americans, but I don't know how it spread to Japan, creating the most mysterious den of vice. In the new Chinese novels with a Japanese flavor, authors always praise the cafés on Tokyo's Ginza Street as being as magnificent as the Guanghan Palace, with waitresses who are as beautiful and knowledgeable. This makes readers imagine what a good place Japanese cafés are. But the reality is very different; they are simply dens of money-wasting.

The development of the café business in Japan is astonishing. Wherever there are bustling streets, such as Ginza, Shinjuku, and Asakusa, they are everywhere. Even in very desolate places, they still have their businesses. There are at least tens of thousands of them in all of Tokyo. The storefronts on the main streets and roads are very expensive and too conspicuous, so they are all located in nearby quiet streets and alleys, with very small frontages, with beautiful and dazzling red lights. Every evening, as the lights come on, the waitresses dress up seductively, waiting for customers at the small entrances, peering and craning their necks.

Ordinary cafés are very small, and even if you arrange them economically, they can only seat a dozen or so people. Small electric lights of various colors emit dim light. The waitresses sit next to the customers, allowing them to tease them. A phonograph is an important tool, playing various intoxicating music, adding auditory stimulation to the senses of sight and taste. The waitresses can all sing, and their clear songs, harmonizing with the phonograph, can really be soul-stirring.

A cup of coffee is at most two jiao, and they can't survive on coffee revenue alone. Their sole purpose is to sell alcohol. A few bottles of beer and foreign wine can be very valuable. Moreover, the price is not fixed. It is very common for two people to spend twenty or thirty yuan on one visit. The waitresses' tips are even more unpredictable, depending entirely on the customers' generosity. But when they encounter stingy customers and the tips are too small, they will play a prank, scattering a handful of salt on you as you leave, indicating that they don't want such patrons to visit again.

Because of the development of cafés in Tokyo, girls from the countryside all run to Tokyo. Other professions are not easy to find. If they are of the right age and have pretty faces, they can go to cafés to work as waitresses. Because the café doors are plastered with advertisements for hiring waitresses all day long, they seem to accept anyone who comes. At the very least, they have graduated from elementary school, and some have graduated from girls' schools. Some people say that even female students above the specialized level enter cafés, but that is extremely rare. They are open for business from the afternoon until 12:00 at night, and they usually have two shifts, taking turns resting. They have to force themselves to smile all day long, accompanying guests drinking and smoking. Their stomachs are full of beer and coffee, cold and hot, which is not a good thing, so they almost don't need to eat, and their stomachs are never hungry.

In addition to their monthly salary, their income usually depends on the customers' tips. Fortunately, they all have their own regular customers, who come to patronize them from time to time, and they can also do side jobs. Otherwise, how can they maintain their frequently changed clothes and household food expenses? Japanese women originally marry very late, and the waitresses are all young girls, so it is very easy for them to fall in love with customers. There are several suicides every day due to heartbreak and marriage problems. Same-sex love is also most common among actresses and waitresses.

Large-scale cafés (sometimes called Western-style bars) have two or three floors, are luxuriously decorated, and can rival game halls and large companies. There are more than two hundred waitresses, each assigned a number, and they hand out small business cards with their nicknames. Customers can freely choose which number to call to accompany them. These types of cafés are relatively proper, and all kinds of food have fixed prices, but the prices are especially expensive. Small plates of snacks for drinking are sold on small carts. A piece of raw tofu and twenty or thirty pods of edamame cost four jiao, which would be enough to buy for forty or fifty wen in a small restaurant in our country. There are also regulations for waitresses' tips, one yuan per person, but additional small tips are, of course, all the better. There are already two or three such large cafés in [location], and they are fully booked every night, with several thousand yuan in daily turnover. Café King Li Qidong is a Korean who made his fortune by running cafés.

Japanese people often criticize Americans for pursuing dancing, drinking, extravagance, and waste. But the bad habits of drinking and drinking coffee in their own country are also very prevalent. This kind of den of vice has gradually been understood by the government and the public. Last year, students were forbidden from entering cafés. Recently, government offices have wanted to drive cafés and Western-style bars in Ginza and Marunouchi out of the country altogether, so this mysterious den of vice will be relocated to a better place.
