Commercial News

Finance: The tight situation on the floor has not eased slightly; bid prices have seen another four yuan increase.

Yesterday, the gold market was as tense as before. Bullish news came from the commodity market. Prices fell and then rose, and buying interest suddenly surged, and the upward trend was especially rapid. Banks worked hard to sell, and international news was not very good and slightly settled. In the morning, the overseas silver market saw the British pound rise and the US dollar remain flat. The forward silver price in Montreal narrowed by one to one and a half li. Exchange rates rose slightly, and London spot gold rose by one penny. The international situation still tended to be bad, and people's minds were still weak. Off-market pending transactions opened, but retreated to 88 yuan. Dade Cheng, Yongli, Huixiang, and Dada immediately sold, and it fell to 6 yuan. Dade Cheng and Hengyu took advantage of the low price to enter at 7 yuan. Fuxing Shui was still selling. The morning opened at a low price. The Central Bank's official exchange rate was announced, with the British pound and the US dollar both flat. The customs gold unit rose by four li, and the standard gold bid price was posted at 920 yuan and 5 jiao. After the opening, it stabilized, but large traders took advantage of the high price to continue selling. Banks were eager to buy, and the exchange rate loosened and gradually went downstream. Knowing in advance that HSBC's official exchange rate would be flat for both the British pound and the US dollar, banks took advantage of the cheap price to buy, and Sassoon also paid in shillings. Buyers began to be active and gradually broke through the 90 yuan mark. Large traders took advantage of the high price to continue selling off, and there was a slight decline. However, the floor was dry and prices were easy to rise but difficult to fall. Sassoon repeatedly demanded, and the domestic market was even tighter. The Central Bank opened for cash, and buying interest was extremely strong, and everything was rising. Large traders continued to sell off in many ways, and the upward trend stabilized slightly. Banks then came to plug the gap, and it fell back. However, the floor was still tight and easy to pull up. Banks were still plugging the gap. The prediction that Indian silver would report a big four anna once weakened. At noon, the situation was stable. The afternoon market immediately started a rising wind. Buyers were continuous, and prices rose due to a lack of supply. Banks took advantage of the high price to sell forcefully. There was news from foreign telegrams that [countries] intended to be at odds, and selling suddenly arose, and it was easy to fall back. Large traders maintained the low price in many ways, but it was still a struggle because Indian silver reported a six anna increase. The Guangdong gang came to buy US dollars, and prices were still easy to pull up after this. Banks sold quickly, and the exchange rate hardened slightly. Indian silver was reported flat a second time, but soon fell again. However, the floor was dry, and the trend was still stable. Large traders continued to sell off, and finally the market fluctuated.

The morning opening was 886 yuan and 6 jiao, a setback of 1 yuan and 8 jiao compared to the previous close. The Central Bank's official exchange rate for customs gold rose by four li. Although Fuxing Yong sold to 6 yuan and 2 jiao, Dade Cheng and Heng entered, rising to 7 yuan. Huixiang, Richang, Yifeng, Yongchunyuan, Yongyuanyi, Hengyu, and Yicheng sold off at high prices. HSBC paid 3.125 shillings for September, falling to 4 yuan and 7 jiao. Yongli, Tongtaichang, Huixiang, and Richang took advantage of the low price to enter at 6 yuan and 1 jiao. Macauli paid 8.75 US dollars for November. Fuxing Yong, Dada Cheng, Yongfeng, Hengyu, Yuqing Yong sold off, falling to 4 yuan and a half. Because its horse woolen, herringbone woolen, and clip coats have a better reputation than other places, imported horse satin sleeves are made. Domestically produced satin palm sleeve satin, because domestic goods are cheap and widely sold, imports have decreased by two-thirds. The goods sold in the market this year are all domestic goods. Yesterday, Tao Hua Jiugong, the gray brand, the horse palm satin wholesale sold for each yard. The wholesale price for the sub-brand was 0.625 yuan, Da Tung 0.645 yuan, and Rui Hua 0.6 yuan. There were also a few miscellaneous brands that sold for only 0.5, 0.4, and 0.7-0.8 yuan.

Oil Market - White Tung Oil Rising Trend Still Fierce -

White tung oil continues to rise and is still in short supply. One or two dozen tons is already considered a large order. The price rose from 70 yuan to 74.5 yuan last week. However, according to the Han telegram yesterday, the price has already been sold at 76 yuan. It is heard that new oil delivered in November-December must also be at 62 yuan. The seat price of the new oil is too high. If foreign firms withdraw their hands in the future, there may be a reaction.

Free Talk

September Season

— Yu

If this is purely theoretical, then it naturally doesn't deserve the amusement of knowledgeable people. If it possesses some historical lessons, then it shouldn't be dismissed as mere scholarly talk. I detest those who exploit the dead, using innocent deceased people as a shield for their crimes. However, some crystallizations of ancient philosophers' thoughts can serve as guidelines for modern people, and certain fragments of past history can be used as lessons for modern people under certain circumstances.

From the perspective of human evolution, large-scale wars between human groups have a long history. In this long historical process, some theoretical tactics gained through experience have been considerably developed and passed down to modern people by any nation with a reasonably long history. Although these experiences have completely changed due to the vicissitudes of the times and the advancement of science, the basic conditions of war have not changed much. Opening the classic "Sun Tzu," which Chinese military strategists have always revered, it tells us, "If victory comes too slowly, weapons are blunted; if the army is exposed too long, the state's resources will be insufficient. When weapons are blunted, morale is dampened, strength is exhausted, and resources are depleted, the other lords will take advantage of the situation and rise up. Even a wise man will not be able to recover from this. "It also says, "Obtain resources from the state, and take supplies from the enemy… A wise general strives to eat from the enemy." It also says, "An army perishes without baggage, perishes without provisions, perishes without accumulated supplies." I believe these principles are still relevant to modern warfare because economic conditions have always occupied a very important position in wars, whether ancient or modern, Chinese or foreign, and are especially important in modern warfare. The military needs of a modern total war are definitely not comparable to the small-scale wars of ancient times, with "a thousand chariots and ten thousand armored soldiers." The "internal and external expenses, the cost of guests, the materials used for glue and lacquer, and the provisions for chariots and armor" of a modern country definitely do not stop at "a thousand gold coins per day" like in ancient times. Therefore, a country without a solid economic foundation and without abundant financial resources cannot wage a long-term war without eventually becoming impoverished and failing. This is a lesson for aggressor nations, and it can also be taken as a source of increased confidence in resistance for nations that are being invaded.

In fact, when a strong and overwhelmingly powerful aggressor invades a nation's territory, "serving them with cattle and sheep," "serving them with hides and coins," and "serving them with pearls and jade" will not be enough to prevent them from taking the entire land. The invaded nation has no choice but to "stake everything they own in one glorious throw." This is not just an emotional reaction, but it has a very important meaning. It means that if an invaded country has the determination to "break the cauldrons and sink the boats" and resist to the point of "mutual destruction" with the enemy, then when it reaches a point of no return, there is no need for the enemy to destroy important cities with airplanes and cannons first. Instead, they should first destroy the sources of wealth that the enemy could use, concentrate on strategic locations, and wage a protracted war, so that "there is nothing to plunder in the fields," and the enemy cannot use their resources to feed themselves. Although the modern nation's military supply preparation is not limited to "single food," and modern transportation is extremely convenient, unlike ancient times when "supplying rations from a thousand miles away caused soldiers to look hungry, and foraging for firewood and cooking after the fact meant the army couldn't eat its fill," but in a country with a vast territory and such inconvenient transportation, and in a prolonged war lasting several years, I don't believe that the enemy's baggage train can keep up with the food supply, or that their accumulated supplies can last without leading to their demise.

Let's use historical examples as proof. In 218 BC, the Carthaginian general Hannibal invaded Rome, and with his talent, he disturbed the Italian territory for fifteen years, and was invincible. In the territory of Etruria, near Lake Trasimene, he wiped out the entire Roman army in that area. In 216 BC, he defeated the army of the Roman general Varro in the Battle of Cannae, killing 50,000 men and capturing 10,000. Although Hannibal failed to conquer Rome due to a lack of siege weapons, the fall of Rome was imminent. However, Hannibal eventually found himself isolated and deep inside enemy territory, with his rear cut off by the Roman general Scipio Africanus. In addition, the Roman general Fabius implemented his "Fabian strategy," avoiding direct confrontation with Hannibal's army, but guarding strategic locations, cutting off Hannibal's supply ships, and attacking Hannibal's scattered troops. Under this kind of protracted war, Hannibal eventually had to withdraw from Italy because Scipio Africanus led his troops to conquer Africa. If history can really be used as a lesson, this is the first historical event with the most instructional significance.

Turning to modern history, we can also find a historical event with extremely instructional significance. That is the history of Napoleon's invasion of Russia and his defeat. We know that Napoleon's defeat after invading Russia from Poland was entirely due to geographical reasons, and not because of poor tactics, because Napoleon had not suffered any defeats before reaching Moscow. Napoleon always thought that after conquering Moscow, Alexander I would sue for peace, but the Russian government would rather burn Moscow than sue for peace, which Napoleon had not anticipated. Not only the government was like this, but also the people were resolutely opposed. When we talk about a section in Tolstoy's "War and Peace," we can know what kind of meaningful passive resistance the Russian people were making at that time.

"Every Russian, not from the deduction of reason, but from the emotions buried deep in our hearts and in the hearts of our ancestors, could know what would happen.

"From Smolensk upwards, in every town and village within Russian territory… the same events were happening, just like in Moscow. The people waited for the enemy's arrival without panic; they showed no excitement; nor did they tear anyone to shreds, but simply waited quietly for their misfortune to come, feeling within themselves a kind of power that would find the methods they ought to find in times of danger.

"And when the enemy was about to come, the richer people fled, leaving their property behind; the poorer people stayed behind and burned everything that was left." (According to Garnett's English translation of "War and Peace")

From this passage, we can see the national spirit of the Slavic people. On the one hand, they burned their property to show their unwillingness to submit. On the other hand, they waited for an opportunity to alleviate their difficulties. When winter arrived, all of Russia was buried in heavy snow, and Napoleon's army finally couldn't bear the hunger, cold, and retreated. These troops turned into hordes of marauders, looting for a living along the way. So, "the Russian peasants, as long as they had weapons, rose up to attack and kill the remnants of his 'Grand Army'." As H.G. Wells said, the retreat of Napoleon's Grand Army was "one of the greatest tragedies" in history.

The British author Joseph Conrad, through the words of an old Russian soldier, vividly described the miserable state of Napoleon's army in retreat:

"That was the first time my comrades and I had a close look at Napoleon's army. It was a strange and terrible sight. …A crowd of crawling, stumbling, hungry, half-mad people. This line emerged from the forest half a mile away, their heads disappearing into the darkness of the field... They offered no resistance. I only heard a few gunshots, perhaps only half a dozen. Their senses seemed to have frozen inside...

"My horse knocked a soldier to the ground. The poor wretch was wearing a blue cavalry uniform, completely torn and scorched, hanging from his shoulders in shreds, and he didn't even reach out to grab my saddle to save his own life. He just fell forward... (J. Conrad: A Warrior's Soul)." Napoleon, the invincible, would never have imagined when he first sent out his troops that the "savage Russians" (Des Russes Sauvages), despised by the French, would give him such a big defeat. If history can really be used as a lesson, this is the second historical event with the most instructional significance.

Finally, we want to talk about historical events that happened not long ago. In some places, these historical events can give people the courage to deal with foreign enemies. During the Russian Civil War, the peasants and those Shock Brigades were of great help in quelling Kolchak, Denikin, and foreign enemies. Their heroic battles were due, on the one hand, to the rape and pillage by the foreign invaders. As soon as the enemy invaded and occupied a school, they would immediately shout "Women! Russian girls, Russian girls!" This naturally aroused the great anger of the Russian people. On the other hand, the main reason was a firm belief. They fully understood the meaning of the war, so even though they knew they would fail, they did not retreat. Levinson, the protagonist in "The Rout" anticipated at the beginning of the war that "we are going to be defeated... certainly." Finally, Levinson broke through the encirclement, although he suddenly felt "...somehow, his whole body suddenly lost strength and withered away. People suddenly felt that he was very weak and very old." However, in the end, he regained his original perseverance. "He looked at the high, distant sky with silent, still moist eyes, this land that gives bread and peace, these distant people in the threshing yard—he should quickly make them all of one mind with himself... so he did not cry: he must live and fulfill his duty. (The above is from Zhou's translation of The Rout)." This epic describing the Russian Civil War truly expresses the main characteristics in the hearts of the Russian people at that time. Therefore, the defeat of Denikin and Kolchak was not accidental. If history can really be used as a lesson for us, this is the third historical event with the most instructional significance.

Finally, I will end with the words of the poet Schiller:

"The most despicable nation is the one that cannot stake all its glory in one throw." (See Guan's translation of The Maid of Orleans.) If you think this is a poet's emotion, this kind of emotion contains a very high meaning. Those people who are full of despondency, who have no ideals, who are rolling around in vulgar utilitarianism, and who are haggling over the weight of a goose feather, naturally will not understand this meaning and will think it is nonsense, so I naturally won't bother to argue with them.

Suicide (2)

— Qian Dong

"I don't remember," Dr. Lan frowned. At this moment, he remembered something, so he waved his hand and exclaimed in annoyance, "Three o'clock!" Then he slowly and impatiently paced back and forth.

The pastor became angry, wiping his face with a handkerchief forcefully. His voice was like thunder, and even the light overhead flickered in surprise:

"How can you forget so easily?"

"Do you know how many suicides have passed through my hands? And their backgrounds are always the same. You only come to see them occasionally, only see one occasionally, so naturally you remember them easily!"

The pastor seemed not to have heard what he said. He was still wiping his nose and thundering, "Can you still forget? When he was taken down from the ambulance, you said it was useless and told the nurse to call and send him to the morgue. Later, the nurse gave him artificial respiration, and when you looked closely again, you said he could still be saved, gave him an injection, and he slowly woke up. That's the one, that's the one!"

"Oh, it seems like there was one. Can he leave today?" Dr. Lan seemed impatient, as if he had mistaken someone, and slowly began to walk.

The pastor became even more excited and energetic, almost rubbing his nose raw. He fumbled in his bag. At this time, he remembered that he hadn't sat down since coming down from the elevator. So he wiped the white bench with his hand, sat down, and put the bag on his lap to rummage through it.

He took out a notebook and flipped to a page in the middle that recorded the patient's growth. He put down the bag and stood up again:

"Look, look, this is his name!"

Yearning

— Hei Ding

—On the Batur and Guyuan Wilderness—

We are hungry, we are hungry!

Let’s go, go quickly, do not fear the cold, do not fear the wind and snow, climb over Songji Mountain, cross the Ergun River—

Leap into the vast Siberian territory. That is a good place,

There is work there, making us so happy.

—The song of the Blagoveshchensk youth is spring.

Spring, on the Batur and Guyuan wilderness, coldness, desolation, and barrenness are still seen everywhere. Snowflakes, clean and radiant with white light, dance and cover the mountains, forests, villages, and still rivers.

The earth is deathly silent. The Batur and Guyuan wilderness is a boundless, desolate desert.

I feel no sorrow. Although I am a fugitive on this snowy Batur and Guyuan wilderness, although my heart has been pierced by countless, tattered, blood-stained holes by the sharp arrows of this wandering and impoverished life, I feel no grief or sadness. Instead, I joyfully stride forward with steps as firm as steel, heading straight towards the place of light on my unfinished path.

I need not worry with nostalgic feelings about the days to come. I know deeply, deeply, that the days to come will be filled with the light of the resurrected sun of death.

Nor do I need to feel lost with nostalgic feelings for the distant homeland that has sunk under the iron heels of oppression. I know even more deeply, deeply, that one day, the compatriots of my homeland will cry out like the eruption of a volcano.

(The sun tore through the thick, heavy clouds in the sky and smiled from afar.)

If life is enough to transform my thoughts, then I am willing to wander forever on this cold and desolate Batur and Guyuan wilderness. Enjoying the active breath of life that fills this wilderness. Wind, snow, hunger, and poverty have conquered me and transformed me into a cold, primitive person. I went deep into the Iktu-ru mountain villages, and I trekked through the valleys of the Ilan Hadayama. Only in the end did I wander to this Batur and Guyuan wilderness.

I spent a warm winter dream here. Now, according to the season, spring has come, but the wilderness is still howling with the angry winds of December. The grasslands, forests, rivers, and streams are as rigid as if they are asleep, and have not yet shown a hint of spring.

Spring, sprout quickly, I need your warm sunshine.

Perhaps Siberia is also covered in hard ice? Perhaps white snowflakes are falling? I finally think so. Thus, I longed for the beautiful dream of Siberia, and my restless and strange fantasies began again. Am I not also being forced by hunger? Whenever I recall the song of the Blagoveshchensk youth and savor it carefully, I am so happy and my heart is filled with encouraging courage, wanting to fly over Songji Mountain, cross the Ergun River, and leap into the vast Siberian territory.

However, I was disappointed—my heart couldn't help but turn cold, like a stagnant pool of forever still, quiet water.

Gazing at the continuous, undulating peaks like a long snake in the Bayanzurkh area east of the Ergun River, I was grieved. Alas, let me, this lonely wanderer, wander aimlessly on this desolate and melancholic Batur and Guyuan wilderness!

Morning in the Suburbs (Part 1)

— Hu Yifan

The sky was still dark, and already there were shadowy figures on the cinder paths of the suburbs. Although one could only see some blurry outlines of the people in front of them, everyone could greet each other with skillful familiarity:

"Morning."

"Oh, morning."

"Business is tough this year."

"Uh-huh, tough."

As usual, everyone nodded, smiled, sighed, exchanged a few brief words, and then ignored each other, going their separate ways.

The shadowy figures slowly dispersed, moving in all directions, sometimes expanding, sometimes shrinking, disappearing. In the fields, in the cotton fields, in the sorghum thickets, in the vegetable gardens, and near the manure pits, these grayish-white dots of activity were scattered everywhere. Everywhere was full of tireless farmers!

Humph yo! Humph yo! Necks stretched straight, teeth clenched tightly, were the small vegetable vendors running on the road. They had gotten up in the middle of the night, carrying their large and heavy loads, and had already run quite a bit of the way.

The rumbling, clattering carts also appeared. They carried fresh flowers for the idle classes in the city to enjoy.

Over there on the cinder road, the carts were being pushed with a "sha-sha-sha" sound, full of wet clothes. The sun had not yet come out, but here, snow-white, crimson, bright yellow-orange, and odd-colored clothes had already been hung up one by one on the large, rough rope racks supported by four bamboo poles. The clothes fluttered proudly on the racks, while the laundry workers below panted heavily.

The milk cart rattled along. The bottles full of milk, squeezed from the cows in the middle of the night, were stacked on the carts and were about to be delivered to the fortunate people to enjoy. The cows were milked until they were limp under the wooden frame of the milk shed, and the milkers were still wearing their white hats and coats!

In a corner under a shed, an old man was gargling, stripped to the waist. He scrubbed back and forth frantically inside his mouth with a yellowed toothbrush, muttering curses.

"Gen fa ge niang, huh, zao la ge niang, clothes are better for young people to wear! Zao la ge niang, such an old age, huh..."

While cursing, he spat a mouthful of dirty water onto the ground. Then he stuck a forefinger into his mouth and scratched over the incomplete row of teeth. Then, with thumb and forefinger pinching his nose, he let out a "whoosh," opened his hand, and a glob of bright green snot landed smack on the opposite peeling wall.

"Zao la ge niang! Such an old age..."

The old man grumbled, hunched over, and added another sentence.

In the empty space to the left of the shed, a small man as thin as a monkey, wearing a faded red bib, held a large bowl of rice porridge, walking and crying. Two streams of snot dripped down.

The old woman hid in a corner and didn't make a sound. She shielded her forehead with her hand, squinted her red eyes, and peeked ahead. Her withered mouth twitched a few times, then she quickly turned her head and spat coldly, before busily resuming her cooking.

The young daughter-in-law had just rushed out the door, the sleep still in the corners of her eyes, one hand clutching a large wooden basin and the other holding a large bundle of dirty clothes. She walked with a pout.

Di...da-da...di...da-da-di...da...

Very early, the bugle was blowing again at the barracks stationed nearby.

Impressions on the Road

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

Sir Otto Niemeyer's Visit to China

— Li Min

Sir Otto Niemeyer of England, who has the mission of investigating the Chinese economy, arrived in China on the 21st, detouring from Japan. Our officialdom should be giving this visiting guest a very warm welcome. We must also say a few words here to express our humble welcome.

Sir Otto Niemeyer's mission in China is to investigate our country's currency system. Why does Sir Otto Niemeyer want to come to China to investigate the currency system? This is because China's currency system is too chaotic, and there is no fixed exchange rate with foreign countries. It must follow the pound or the dollar at any time. Especially since the United States raised the price of silver, China's currency system has been in a state of chaos. Therefore, Britain is very concerned and sent Sir Otto Niemeyer to China to see what the situation is. The purpose is to get the Chinese silver dollar to follow the pound, and not to be indecisive and subject to the control of other countries at any time. This is Sir Otto Niemeyer's true intention in coming to China. In other words, Britain wants to control China in terms of currency, so that China will become its dependency in terms of currency. This is very clear, the current currency wars of various countries are an important strategy in the struggle for imperialism. China is likely to become a vassal of the US dollar at any time, so Britain naturally cannot help but want to change China's currency system.

This can be said to be an important mission of Sir Otto Niemeyer's visit to China today. From behind Sir Otto Niemeyer, we can clearly see the complex background of the various countries fighting each other for China. Whether Sir Otto Niemeyer's visit to China is really helpful to China is still a question, but the fact that China is now a piece of meat on the chopping board has already become a reality. This is one aspect.

Secondly, Sir Otto Niemeyer originally planned to come to the United States first, but then he suddenly changed his route, and came to China from Japan, China's eastern neighbor, instead of the United States. From this we can see how Britain is trying to increase the friendly relationship between Britain and Japan. The rapprochement between Britain and Japan indicates that the two countries may have a growing consensus on China. This clearly shows that the recent tensions in the European political situation have led Britain to rely on the strong countries in the Far East in mutually beneficial conditions, so naturally, China is again the first to bear the brunt.

Therefore, today, the general public is welcoming Sir Otto Niemeyer's visit to China with twelve points of awe, while laughing bitterly. How much benefit will this trip of Sir Otto Niemeyer's bring to China, which can no longer be squeezed any further? We have no way of knowing. We can only hope that the nations can be forgiving and not keep drawing swords on us. This point is already an unexpected joy that cannot be hoped for.

Road

— Family

Starting several months ago, on the official road outside the West Gate of the county town, every day, one could often see a group of people, one with a badge on his chest, wearing thick-rimmed glasses, followed by two or three assistants. Some carried a "Luopan" compass, and some carried bamboo poles with red flags, patrolling back and forth on the official road. From this side to that side, first the person wearing glasses and a Zhongshan suit opened the "Luopan" compass, took out a pen, and compared and drew here and there on the paper. Afterwards, the assistants would stick the flag on the ground and then go back. They would come again the next day, always those few people, always that same routine. The people living nearby saw this every day, and they really felt a bit strange, but no one knew what it was all about. It seemed someone said they were surveying the foundation, and the official road was soon to be widened for cars.

But why did it have to be so cumbersome, taking months to get done? They really couldn't figure it out. However, when the topic of building a road was mentioned, they were very insightful and cleverly associated it with some troublesome matters. Especially many small shops facing the road. Everyone knew that their houses would be

Page 18

torn down. Once torn down, they would have to be rebuilt, but what would they use to rebuild? That was something to worry about.

"You know, there will also be road construction fees and…"

When talking about it, some would explain it like this. If it came from the mouths of people from small shops facing the street, their faces would surely be wearing a worried expression.

"The county government's notice has already been posted!"

That evening, Chen Laoqi, the owner of the tea shop on the long street, came back from the city and told his neighbors a piece of worrying news.

"What does the notice say?" Someone asked urgently.

Chen Laoqi stood in front of his shop, illuminated by the dim light, and recited in a heavy tone: "The notice tells us shopkeepers to dismantle our shops voluntarily within a limited time. If we don't dismantle them after the deadline, people will be sent to enforce it forcefully." Those listening looked at each other with expressionless eyes. No one answered, and after a while, they silently dispersed.

As for Chen Laoqi, he didn't get a wink of sleep that night, because his shop had just been newly built a few months ago, and now it had to be destroyed and rebuilt. The year was bad, so what should he do…?

Three days later, the entire road was turned upside down by countless road construction workers. Piles of soil looked like small hills. Some were carrying baskets, some were crushing stones to prepare for paving the road, and some were digging ditches.

The shops on both sides were also being demolished one after another. On the long street, everything was messy and noisy, and it was almost impossible to imagine that the road could be blocked.

Those who delayed dismantling also finally had to dismantle.

In between all of this, there were as many as two or three months, or even half a year. Every shop was stuck in a state of half doing business and half being suspended. Expenses, however, could not be reduced by half a penny. On the one hand, they still had to pay various fees and levies, and on the other hand, they had to raise money to build new houses. In short, it was like getting through a difficult time.

Half a year later, the road was finished, but it was just filled with mud and sand in a slipshod manner. Whenever it rained, there were puddles everywhere, muddy and unbearable. When cars drove past, they always splashed a burst of sewage in all directions. The amount of various donations and fees that many shops paid seemed not small, but the result was just this kind of road. Everyone was naturally upset in their hearts.

As for the shops on both sides, those that were torn down were already torn down, but not many were rebuilt. As a result, the street became a weird, crooked, and dilapidated mess. Moreover, many shops simply closed their doors. Some time ago, this official road was originally very lively, but now it was very deserted. Walking there evoked a different kind of feeling.

The completion ceremony of the highway was held, and then traffic began to flow. People traveling long distances had cars to travel in, and when they were in a hurry to get home at dusk, they naturally felt very convenient. But some others suffered, and no one thought about it. Because the road was not solid and was completed hastily, the cars trampled on it, and the weak places gradually sank, while some places rose up. Adding a few heavy rains, the road became as rugged as a hillside. When cars drove on it, they swayed like boats floating in water. In severe cases, they would overturn, and accidents happened almost all the time. With a sudden diversion, the car body would jump up and drive straight into the shop, or perhaps kick straight past the bodies and stomachs of pedestrians before lying down. As a result, no one knew how many times car accidents had killed people, even though the highway had only been open for two or three months.

Vegetable Vendor A Wu

— Hua Zhi

Speaking of vegetable vendor A Wu, he was somewhat famous in this market. He lived in Zhutiegou, more than ten li outside the city. Every day, he carried a full basket of vegetables to this market, arriving when the market was at its busiest. A Wu was not the only one doing vegetable business in this market; Since A Wu was famous, the other vegetable vendors could only resist by coming to the market early. But it was useless. The officials and gentry "ate fame". A Wu's vegetables were good, and they had to wait for A Wu. Therefore, before A Wu's vegetables were sold out, the other vegetable vendors couldn't expect to attract a customer.

"Hmph, A Wu's vegetables are fertilized with manure, and our vegetables are also fertilized with manure. It's not that his manure tastes particularly good!"

When those vegetable vendors couldn't do business, they deliberately raised their voices to satirize the "basket-carrying" customers. But the "basket-carrying" people were under orders from their masters. Their masters wanted to eat A Wu's vegetables, and they had no choice but to buy A Wu's vegetables. Although they heard those even filthier sarcastic remarks every day, they still rushed to buy A Wu's vegetables.

Seeing that business was good, A Wu brought out more vegetables every day. The vegetable business in this market was almost exclusively managed by him. In this way, there were no peaceful days in the market. At first, everyone fought verbally, and later, fights often occurred. Speaking of fighting, A Wu also had some skills, but the other vegetable vendors united, and A Wu was no match. Moreover, they came up with various methods to deliberately make trouble; Waiting for A Wu to carry the vegetables out, they would provoke him on the way. If A Wu retorted, the two sides would wrestle and fight, and the bystanders would dump his vegetable basket into the mud ditch.

A Wu had not been able to do business for several days. So he thought of a way to run to the officials' residences. Every day, he carried vegetables to the government offices, which the other vegetable vendors could not prohibit. However, there was still some good business to be done in the market.

On A Wu's side, he also had a special advantage, which was that he didn't have to share the profits with the "basket-carrying" middlemen. He could sell at a better price to the old gentlemen and ladies who liked to "eat fame." Although he let go of many customers, his income would not decrease.

But after a few months, A Wu's business scope became smaller and smaller. This was not because the other vegetable vendors had come up with any other methods to destroy him, but because A Wu himself was lazy. He always stayed in the homes of several familiar officials and gentry, chatting with the maids and cooks, chatting for a long time about everything under the sun. Sometimes, he would even help them with their chores. If people casually invited him to eat, he would sit at the table without any politeness, leaving the several officials' residences that he was supposed to deliver to behind. In this way, A Wu lost his credibility, and his customers gradually shifted to the other vegetable vendors in the market.

A Wu abandoned his good business, and his small fame made people suspicious; Especially the other vegetable vendors who were hostile to him. In the market, everyone would talk about this matter intentionally or unintentionally. Those "basket-carrying" people also let slip, saying: "Everyone's vegetables are the same, it's not like A Wu's are watered with ginseng soup!"

The vegetable vendors were pleased to do business:

"A Wu's manure is more fragrant than ours!"

Every day, A Wu was the center of conversation in the market.

But what was A Wu thinking? One day, a shocking new rumor spread through this small city—he had abducted a maid from an official's residence and fled.

The discussion in the market was:

"A Wu's vegetables are good? A Wu's ability to abduct women is even better!" While busy tying vegetables, the vegetable vendors echoed each other and laughed.

Typhoon

— Lin Xi

In my hometown, typhoons are called "fengtai" (wind storm). A letter came from home saying that my hometown was hit by a typhoon again, and my worries were confirmed. For many days, newspapers had repeatedly published news of typhoons passing through, saying that the South Sea area had already been hit. At that time, I was very concerned about my hometown. I was thinking, don't let there be another typhoon again. I prayed for my hometown. Who knew that my suspicion would be confirmed? A letter came from home saying that many coconut trees had been blown down. The half-ripened rice ears were blown down in one direction, drooping and soaking in the water.

Typhoons are common in my hometown. They often occur between August and September. Hurricanes flying from the Philippines often blow through the northeast corner of my hometown, and then blow along the coast towards Taiwan to the east. Small typhoons are nothing much. If they are big, there will be disaster. Blowing down coconut trees is not much of a loss. Blowing away the rice and blowing away the roof tiles is a big loss. I remember there was a really big typhoon one year. I was still young at that time, and the wind blew so hard that I didn't dare to go out. I couldn't stand still. I really couldn't stand still in the wilderness. Coconut leaves more than ten feet long flew all over the sky, destroying many houses! Almost every household suffered. I remember the thatched hut of Black Auntie next to the village was crushed by a fallen coconut tree. Her little grandson, who was eight or nine years old, a child who had no parents from the moment he was born, was so pitiful, and died in the rubble pile! This destroyed Black Auntie's lifeline. No one would continue the ancestral incense. Although Black Auntie escaped from danger, she went crazy. She pointed to the sky and cursed all day long, with tears in her eyes. Now, the house that has been mostly collapsed is still there, and Black Auntie is still guarding that half-collapsed house, living a life that is neither alive nor dead, passing the days in prayer and cursing. Such a half-mad old woman is really miserable. When I think of her, I also point to the sky and curse. This makes me very afraid and concerned about my hometown. Don't let there be another flying disaster. I pray for my hometown.

Of course, if the wind blows too hard, every household will suffer, but small typhoons are quite interesting. Maybe it's because I felt it was very interesting when I was a kid and I liked it very much. Small typhoons don't cause much loss. This is quite like what someone said about illness; He said that one shouldn't be too sick, because if it's too bad, it's dangerous, and at least it will make your body and mind suffer enough. Small illnesses are interesting: there is not much loss, and you can also eat some good things and nourish yourself. This is great: you just lie down and browse some light publications, look at the various medicine bottles, and feel that little bit of desolate taste, which is quite poetic; saying that this is quite happy, I think maybe it's right. Typhoons are also like this. Small typhoons are quite interesting.

Small typhoons can even be said to be "fengli" (wind encouragement), but they are different from ordinary wind and rain, so they are called "fengtai" (wind storm). The difference is probably not in the size of the wind and rain, but in the taste. Typhoons have a typhoon taste. For example, tsunamis, with low and fast clouds, must be said to have a typhoon taste. Ordinary wind and rain may not have such a prelude. Tsunamis sound like muffled thunder from afar, with a deep and dull sound that is regular, sometimes far and sometimes near, and also a bit like hearing the sound of a large waterfall in the distance. Old people can hear the size of the typhoon from this sound. They understand the signs of the typhoon, and they are more worried than ordinary people. Watching the coconut leaves dance and listening to the sound of the tsunami, whether it is a small typhoon or a flying disaster, they are rarely happy. "The tsunami is very urgent," they worryingly look at the sky, and then they will calculate the harvest and hope that the clouds are thinner; Thinner, so that they can keep more hope in their hearts. Indeed, if the typhoon is smaller, their happiness is really hard to describe, just like getting back a lost and recovered valuable item. Their happiness is really not comparable to getting a small illness. This is the mood of the elderly. My liking for small typhoons is not calculated from the harvest; children's hearts are not willing to be lonely, and they want to play. Small typhoons will satisfy them. I remember when I was a child, when I occasionally encountered a small typhoon, I would often be so excited that I couldn't sleep at night, and I would even light a lantern in the middle of the night to pick up coconuts in the coconut grove. Thinking about it, this is very interesting. Hearing the sound of a coconut falling to the ground from afar, chasing the wind and storm, following the sound to find a rather heavy thing in the small bushes, this is a fun thing in the eyes of children. This is one thing. There are many more reasons to like small typhoons, such as listening to the sounds of nature on windy and rainy nights, watching the clouds and flowing water during the day, and the sky full of flying bamboo leaves, like swallows coming in spring; these things are deeply ingrained in my memory. Speaking of it, small typhoons are still gentle and friendly things.

But this time it's terrible, not so gentle. I'm afraid what's flying is not bamboo leaves but bamboo poles with roots. The letter from home only mentioned rice, and that's sad enough; although it may not be a flying disaster of flying tiles and collapsing houses, it seems that many people should be blaming the year again. But as long as it's not a flying disaster, it's still good.

Opening chapter "Li Taibai"

In the past, Xichuan descended to the immortal. The long star entered the dream and produced Yingxian. Talent like the sea and writing like silk. Drunk crazy singing hundreds of poems. Thoughts on "The Storm" and the Like

— Wei Heling

I played a father in "The Beginning of Man," and I also play a father in "The Storm," as if I were born to be a father. In "The Beginning of Man," I had a lawsuit; in "The Storm," my family was ruined. Both were suffering fathers. Truly, in these hard times, being a father is difficult!

"The Storm" is staged in this peaceful autumn, but is the world as peaceful as this autumn?

On a gloomy day like this year's Mid-Autumn Festival, "The Storm" is perhaps more interesting than the silent, gossamer-like, and reticular drizzle!

Some people ask me my thoughts on acting in "The Storm," but I want to know what people think of "The Storm" in their hearts.

In these days of national peril, "The Storm" may not be entirely meaningless. I hope it can stir up a "storm" a little bigger than this in the hearts of sweet, drunken men and women, and then I will be satisfied.

I am waiting for a very blunt but serious criticism.

Recent News from the Oriental Drama Society

The Oriental Drama Society, sponsored by the Moonlight Film Company, received over a thousand letters within five days of advertising for members. After reviewing and testing, Wan Laitian and Jin Shan, the two responsible persons, were busy day and night. Now the deadline has passed. According to Mr. Wan, the final decision will be made within days. The allocation of the twenty positions will be approximately twelve men and eight women. They will soon be notified to join the society for training, with the Moonlight Company fully providing room and board. It is also heard that their first public performance will be at a charity carnival, with the script already decided as "The Mute Wife" by [the French playwright] Frantosto.

A Souvenir of a European Tour

— Hu Die (Butterfly Wu)

"Night Blooming Cereus" is a very good souvenir for me personally.

Filming for "Night Blooming Cereus" began last winter. When it was only half finished, I had to put it on hold because I was going abroad to participate in the Soviet International Film Festival. It wasn't until I returned from my five-month European tour that I resumed work, and now the whole film is finally completed. —— I have unknowingly developed a great fondness for "Night Blooming Cereus" because it can be considered my European tour souvenir.

As for my acting in this film, although I worked harder and tried harder, I dare not say that I have achieved particularly good results. Naturally, after traveling to Europe, my horizons have broadened a lot, and my knowledge has also increased a lot; but to say that my acting has suddenly improved in a short time because of this trip would not be true. I only have this confidence: to use my life experience, the knowledge I gained from my travels, and sincere effort to enable my acting to make new progress.

Now "Night Blooming Cereus" is about to be released, and I look forward to the strict instructions of the audience. (This article is a retyped manuscript sent by Star [Film Company])

Shen Bao Local Supplement - Automobile Weekly

The Achievement of Lihe Fearless Charcoal Vehicle is Excellent

— Fu

Mr. Maddy, General Manager of the American Maddy Motor Company, and Mr. Li Baohe of the China Coal Gas Machine Manufacturing Plant, in view of the great importance of using charcoal instead of oil, have made every effort to engage in research and exploration, hoping to improve and perfect it. Fortunately, it has been a great success. In the future, if the highways of various provinces use this new product as a means of transportation, in terms of economics, its cheapness and cost-effectiveness, compared with the use of gasoline, will be vastly different. Moreover, using charcoal as fuel will prevent money from flowing out, which is especially beneficial to the national economy.

This new product is a charcoal-for-oil furnace mounted on a specially constructed Lihe freight vehicle, named the Lihe Fearless Freight Vehicle. After repeated tests, it has been proven that this type of vehicle, whether in terms of economy or roadworthiness, has achieved excellent results. Its cost is less than one-fifth of that of gasoline. The Hunan Provincial Highway Bureau also used this vehicle for testing, and the results were very satisfactory and praised repeatedly. Recently, when the test was held in this city, Mr. Chen Ticheng of the Highway Department of the National Economic Commission also sent a letter of commendation, praising it not only for adding luster to charcoal vehicles, but also for opening a ray of dawn for the future of our country's highways.

The picture shows the Lihe Fearless Charcoal Vehicle. A group photo of the people who participated in the test held in this city recently. In the picture, from left to right, the third person is Mr. Pang Shite of the Mechanical Engineering Department of Lihe Automobile Company, the fourth person is Mr. Li Baohe, the sixth person is Mr. Chen Ticheng, Director of the Highway Department of the Economic Commission, and the eighth person is Mr. Maddy.

Statistics of Road Vehicle Accidents in the United Kingdom

— Yu

Pedestrians should bear half the responsibility

The issue of responsibility for road vehicle accidents. At first glance, it seems that drivers should bear more responsibility. But the fact is not always the case. According to the British Ministry of Transport, based on the road accidents obtained at the beginning of this year, and after careful analysis, it is known that pedestrians should also bear half the responsibility for vehicle accidents. It is not necessarily all the fault of the driver. The Ministry took a total of 1,500 accident cases for analysis and research. 2,532 people lost their lives as a result. Among them, pedestrians who should be held responsible for the accidents accounted for 49.1% of the total. Drivers accounted for only 25.1%. Most of the accidents (accounting for 65.5% of the total) occurred in open roads in urban areas and at easily visible turns. (Accounting for 61.2%) The analysis of the accidents is as follows. Accidents attributed to pedestrians accounted for 736 cases, accounting for 49.1% of the total. Drivers 376 cases, accounting for 25.1%. Cyclists 239 cases, accounting for 15.9%. Vehicles and their accessories 56 cases, accounting for 3.7%. Animals 19 cases, accounting for 1.3%. Weather 15 cases, accounting for 1.0%. Passengers, etc. 15 cases, accounting for 1.0%. Road conditions 8 cases, accounting for 0.5%. The first 736 accident cases mentioned above should be the responsibility of pedestrians. However, these pedestrians all died in the disaster, and it is impossible to obtain any evidence of what happened at the time of the accident.

The reasons for road vehicle accidents caused by the negligence of pedestrians, drivers and cyclists are analyzed as follows. (1) For pedestrians. Crossing the road, obviously not paying attention to traffic conditions 232 cases. Carelessness 23 cases. Hesitation and delay 38 cases. Running out from the front or back of the car, not closely observing the movement of vehicles, 157 cases. Running into the road 84 cases. (2) For drivers (excluding cyclists). Excessive speed 113 cases. Obviously not paying attention 43 cases. Not keeping close to the side of the road 35 cases. Following a car illegally 28 cases. For cyclists. Emerging from a small road to a main road, or crossing a main road without paying attention, 36 cases. Turning from a main road to a small road without paying attention 13 cases. Following a car illegally 31 cases. Pedestrians are responsible for the death of drivers in only 1.5% of cases. These drivers were all riding motorized bicycles. Drivers are responsible for the death of pedestrians in 11.4% of cases. On the other hand, the responsibility of drivers for the death of passengers in sidecars or sidecars reached 78.6%. Other passengers 56.7%

Of the 857 pedestrians who died, 259 (30.2%) were under the age of 15. 423 (49.4%) were 55 years of age and older. The most dangerous age for children is 5 years old (43 deaths). 6 years old (34 deaths). and 7 years old (33 deaths). The most dangerous age for adults is between 65 and 70 years old. (99 deaths) The most common cause of dangerous accidents for children is "running into the road." A total of 77 cases. "Emerging from the front or back of the car without closely observing the movement of vehicles." A total of 67 cases. Other analyses are as follows. (1) Those who died in the accident. Pedestrians 857 people, accounting for 55.9%. Cyclists 310 people, accounting for 20.2%. Motorized bicycle riders 198 people, 12.9. Passengers, etc. 95 people, 6.2. Drivers other than motorized bicycle riders 72 people, 4.8. (2) The nature of the accident. Vehicle collisions and collisions with pedestrians 842 cases, accounting for 56.1% of the total. Moving vehicle collisions 403 cases, 26.9. Those not caused by collisions 123 cases, 8.2. (3) The place where the accident occurred. Open straight roads and easily visible turns 918 cases, accounting for 61.2% of the total. At road intersections 456 cases, 30.4. 29 accident cases occurred at intersections with police direction or traffic lights. (3) Analysis of each car involved in the accident. Private cars accounted for 588 cases, accounting for 29.7% of the total. Motorized bicycles 275 cases, 13.9. Public streetcars 175 cases, 8.8. Large cars and freight cars 479 cases, 24.2. Bicycles 403 cases, 20.3. Horse-drawn carriages 41 cases, 2.1. Two-thirds of all bicycle riders, a total of 95 people, were under the age of 20. One was a four-year-old child. Riding a tricycle. In addition, 77 were boys. 18 were girls. Most of the cyclists (57.7%) died during the day. According to the analysis of the time, the most dangerous time of day is between 5 pm and 7 pm. 11% of all accidents occurred between 5 and 6 o'clock. 10.2% occurred between 6 and 7 o'clock. 183 accident cases occurred between 11:30 pm and 1:00 am. At that time, it was the time when honking the horn was prohibited in the urban area. 48 cases occurred in the urban area. The total number of accidents that occurred in the urban area was 65.5.

In the nine weeks up to August 3rd, 1,088 people died in vehicle accidents and 50,428 were injured. During the same period in 1934, the former was 1,473 and the latter was 52,942. In the 31 weeks since December 30th last year, 3,590 British people have died under vehicles and 124,494 have been injured. During the same period, the number of deaths in the metropolitan area was 638 and the number of injuries was 31,568.
